O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latest work of the science of medicine, embracing its employment in its entirety, and I have finished it through its expositions and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to pass that I realized I must accomplish this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely surgery
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is far-flung in our region and is rare in all, if it is not learned and practiced, and if it is not refreshed, the science and art of it are lost, and nothing remains of it but the little descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this is the source of error and idleness, and the minds are closed and the science is confused.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I can give life to this treatment in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the cautery instruments, and other implements of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary. And because none of our masters of hands can be found in our time, the art of medicine is prolonged
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who undertakes this should be well versed in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he understands the structure of the limbs, the shapes and joints and separations of bones, and knows the bones and nerves and muscles and joints, and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of them, and their issues.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates said that one should not go against the natural order, but follow its work; and the same in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say in the beginning of this book that he who is ignorant of the things that are before him will err and harm others; as I have often seen more of those who get in the way of this science and abandon its science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a madman who copped a scrophule or the head of a woman, and copped the arteries of the neck; so that so much blood flowed out that the woman died between her hands
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another madman who treated a stone of a sick man, and the stone was great; so he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and he was left half-dead for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I am already being called to deal with it, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and know well if one should cut deeply into it, for it would surely kill him.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see also another marvel that takes hold of us from our land, which had its limb broken, and with a splint put on the wound; and the physicians of our land do not know how to handle it, for they leave the wound open without any bandage, and leave it to finish; and they command that it be left alone; and when the limb is completely healed and the bone is fractured, it is lost forever.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come and take it away, and when I arrive I find it dislocated and feeling no pain.</start_of_turn>
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way corruption has already confirmed or member, and does not cease to heal; and it continues corrupting as long as the limb is entirely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another wrinkle that undermines the flesh, enflames and burns from the malice of its lord
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a wound caused by melancholy humours does not suffice except for touching it with iron when it is not in any other part of the body where it can remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, very often, hands are split, knowing that there is peril in more things.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For indeed it is necessary that you keep your hands close to your body, lest the fool should speak maliciously of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you keep your arms close to your body, and undertake your ailments lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that by the grace of God you may come out well; and leave the diseases that are born of grief far behind; and stay away from those things that make you doubt, and have confidence in your heart so that you can go from this world to the next in peace.</start_of_turn>
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	He speaks in vain of his warnings: “Do not take me for a madman in my cure for the disease, for I am not called a fool.”
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to two chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre. The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things; and it is ordered from the head down to the toes, and the forms of instruments.</start_of_turn
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	When we remember our works, it is clear that I must say the quality of the help and the danger of neglecting certain complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the help and the danger are the longest word and the subtlest science and the most secret response; and concerning this, many speak and agree with this; but I am stifled by these words, for I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for any complexion or where there is matter, for there are two complexions: that is to say a complexion hot with matter, and a complexion dry with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexion together matter, some say that the cautery is a great aid; and others say the opposite: that the cautery is of no use in diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.

Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And you must all understand and agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know that fire cautery is more effective for certain secrets than burning cautery.</start_of_turn>
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know then, child, that it is fitting in what way the cauteries should be performed and when they are urgent.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is permissible in all tenses, for the harmful substances that arise are driven out by the aid of the cautery; and even if the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait until the greater harm has passed from the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	Do not think of the fire cautery as a mere trifle, dear son; for in the disease which is cured by it, there is no remission; and he says so himself.  However, it is not so simple, for cautery is but a medicine which changes the complexion, and dries up humors which are the cause of pain; and it is worth more than medicine for its promptness of action, and for the excellence of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And indeed, there is something else which must be known: the disease does not arise once only according to the complexion of the patient and the cause of the disease and its power; and there are assembled in him the superfluous humors by the acquisition of meats and other things, if these are not cauterized either in their entirety or because of pain, and the superfluous humors and moisture, for indeed the pain does not return otherwise; but this is often the case.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that truly cautery is not called medicine; and behold; but they do not believe that it is worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, for indeed it is cautery which is the last resort in any disease for which other remedies are useless.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Although the cautery is often used as the last resort in medicine, it does not suit the understanding of the fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old people say that gold cautery is useless as iron, and they say that fire is only good for its quality of gold and its height; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not make a wound, but I do not believe this, for I have seen it in many people; and gold cautery is worth no more than iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is charred by the color of the gold, and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much; it is burned out.

dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are useful for moisture and cold on the skull, and there are two methods to use them because of the disease called “soda,” and because of the many humors that descend from the head to the ears, and for many dreams and pain of the teeth and throat, and even for all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis, soda and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient is purged by a medicinal solution modifying the head, i.e. nose or mouth, according to what is useful and agreeable to the patient's custom; and then repeat the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his stomach; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his nail between his two thumbs; and there or will come your two middle fingers, if he bleeds from the nail then evacuate the cautery which is called "olive", for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and make descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then take your hand away from the wound element, and renew the cautery until you see the bone even; after that take up one-third of the cautery, and place in awe and soak cotton inside, and take out the cautery, and leave it for two days; after that put on a soft bandage. Leave on until the scab has become solid; then cure the wound of the wound which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they say the old folks, that when it remains longer open the wound, the more it purges; and for this reason it helps the pus.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say none of these that we must leave the cautery on for so long that part of the bone is scorched, and then we must renew that which is scorched from the bone, and be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say another that we must leave the cautery on so long as we must, and press so hard that we break off a piece of the bone as wide as a woman puts in her sleeve for fear of the humors coming out too much; and we must leave the wound open for a long time; after that we must cure and bandage.</start_of_turn
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be sufficient in all cases, for in some men or when there is fear; and I believe that I must leave it; for the head of the shoulder is easily dislocated by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and even when the patient’s head is weak by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more severe and painful for me, and for this reason I will abstain from it.</start_of_turn
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut. Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the shoulder there is sudden pain, and it is extended by the disease, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by means of medicines that alter, and other cures have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this has not profited: then make cauteries according to two methods, that is to say with medicine and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of medicine if it is that you take an alum plant, and oste the bark and cover. That is to say that if there are two heads, and then make the temple where the pain is held in some way that you can restore the alum plant from the skin; and when it is restored if you bind and strain it well and leave it for .xij. hours; and then take it out and treat the alum plant with oil, and leave the wound for .ij. days or .iij.; then put on a soft bandage as much as the situation requires.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the wound is cured while it is still sound; and if you see that it does not respond to any of the medicines I have written or if you wish to treat it with other medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is as follows. Shape the cautery like this:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "closed" because its head is made in the shape of a scoop or has a little curve, and has in the middle a small protrusion; and put out the painful limb, and hold your hand steady and touch the burn with a slight movement, until half of the thickness of the burn is charred; and keep your hand away from the artery, which is blistered, and there is copious bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine. de emigraine	After having put on cotton wool around the limb for two days, and having taken it out; then I put on moist cotton wool in the hole, and finally treat the limb for swelling until it is healed; and if you cauterize this embolism with the cautery called “cultellare,” at its tip, and keep the artery in this embolism from being cut that is not ancient.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cauterize an embolism as we have seen previously in divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery must precede medical treatment and that it does not suffice, then you must avoid the cautery called “cultellare” until it is soft; and when you take out the limb, mark out a line half an inch long with your finger, and hold your hand once, and strain that you do not cut the artery and that it does not bleed excessively; and be careful of the jaw that it does not move when you move it, and that the patient does not feel any pain except for the spasm and the swelling that comes with the disease; and be careful of a discharge of blood from the artery when it is cut, or that there is great fear and distress about that which the patient does not understand, and which is not studied or experienced; and leave the work in peace; but I will tell you later how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	If you see that this cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the surrounding area just as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has 1.5 cuts; and this cautery is better than the former and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	If you see that this cautery does not suffice for the ailment, and the patient is suffering, cauterize the surrounding area just as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see that, administer the cautery that we have said or the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has 1.5 cuts; and this cautery is better than the former and more helpful.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the ear suffers from cold, and there has been no success with soluble medicines and other cures that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then you must apply this cautery which is called the "point," as follows:

de la torture de la bouche	After pricking all around the painful ear, or around the joints if the pain persists in both, and you have loosened the earlobe from the root of the ear as soon as you have signed the mark; and there are ten points around the earlobe; after that, cure the ear until it is healed.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is not fierce except for those which arise from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make any cautery which has the appearance of coming from dryness and swelling of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture that is made of fumes of hydras and vomiting of head and gargling, know that it is worth doing only if you cauterize the patient with two cautery instruments: one at the root of the ear, and the other at the temple, and the third between the two eyebrows; and put the cautery on the part that is open to the air, and make the cautery place where the head of the ear lies below the hollow of the ear, and another at the temple as long as a bean; and leave the cautery in place until half of the current is consumed. This is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When we showed the cutellar to you, it was with a less sharp and more subtle instrument; but it is better that the knife be thicker. Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it as we have said, and it brings no benefit, and the patient has no fever, then you must make three cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one to empty the head, and one at the place which is called "vasselz," as we have said before, and the last cautery on the back of the stomach; and be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	From idleness
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	From idleness, it is appropriate to give the patient large doses of wine and nourishing food; after which the physician should place his hand on the patient’s head and put on the occiput a plaster of rue which is written or treated with plasters; and that is the method of the cautery: as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is well, well he is; if not, two cauteries are made on the head as far as the collarbone, leaving space between each cautery about the size of two thumbs; and the wound is treated like the others. And if you see that it is necessary and the patient is suffering, one cautery is made in the middle; and if there are several, two more on the two horns, and the wound is made until he is well; or the cautery which is called the olive, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the cold of the head

Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant. Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent. And if afterwards the hair comes out, and the marrow is softened, then restart the cautery on that very place as you did before; and if the hair is pulled out, if the cautery is done until the marrow returns to its natural position, and is even, and does not prick the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you command the patient to let the hairs be long and even, and then make parchment of the shape of a laurel leaf; then take French soap and live charcoal, each a third, and grind them together well; and make it frothy, if it does not cool, and put on the shape that you have made like the laurel leaf, and put on the marrow some eggs; and if the patient feels pain only in one oil, you must open in one, and if in both at the same time; and put on the oil cotton moist in egg-white; and the patient’s head should be in its normal position and put your thumb showing on the medicine, and press it once or twice every time the patient feels pain from the medicine, for he feels pain in the same way as from fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have performed this for a long time, if the bones of the medicine are to your credit.

And know that the ears of men are diverse in size, and according to that, their constraints are different; and do not be answered by the straight way to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	And know that the ears of men are diverse in size, and according to that, their constraints are different; and do not be answered by the straight way to him who studies this art.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your cure does not profit, then you must cauterize according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head in your safety; and hold his ear between your hands in part so that it does not move, do not let him lower his head; then put a soaked cotton swab in the ear of oil or vinegar; then burn the cautery which is partly: and is shaped like a goose feather; grasp it with the tweezers so that it is against the ear as if it were a goose feather; if you see that it is too deeply pierced from one ear to the other, or if you see that it is as if a tent; but in any case, what is grasped is better than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells over, and in the course of the process, the pus and the dry matter are evacuated; and if it closes, if the wound is raw, and if there is fire in the wound, take off the bow; then put on the hot cautery, and hold your hand over the part without feeling pain towards the thumb, that your hand does not tremble; put the cautery in the fat of the oil, and press it down.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start with the cautery up to the bone, that would be good. If that does not suffice, repeat the cautery once more, and if you are skilled, leave it in for two days; then put on a moist bandage and treat the drying discharge until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is still not healed, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and withdraw according to what comes to light in your chapter.</start_of_turn>
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way of cautery for fistula that none of the ancients said. In the fistula, and make an opening; then put in between the layers one half of a barleycorn of alum, which is the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I make the quantity of a third of a plum; and hold your hand or arm firmly, and the patient does not move at all, only the melted plum does not return to its oil; and it is good to put on the oil to the patient a soft cotton wad in a box or in a basin. The plum is so apt to rise like a fistula, and to restore health marvelously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, that is good. If not, if it is necessary, it is good to administer mercury to the vein, and restore the fistula to its place according to what is convenient in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	wounds in the liver
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there occur cracks in the limbs which are called "hair", and sometimes in the limbs of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have said in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you should burn [the area around the crack] with a small cautery knife according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And hold it firmly in those cracks until it becomes juice; after curing the limb until it is whole again.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the armpit.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the root of the tooth comes loose in the gums or in the socket, or in the palace, or has the root of the teeth, after that it makes pus and becomes rancid and is filled with pus and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in division, and it does no good: therefore you must cauterize it according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and keep your hand over it until life returns to its original place; and do so once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you must do in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the root of the tooth comes loose in the gums or in the socket, or in the palace, or has the root of the teeth, after that it makes pus and becomes rancid and is filled with pus and becomes a fistula; and you must cure it as we have said in division, and it does no good: therefore you must cauterize it according to the quantity of the fistula; after that drain or perforate the fistula, and keep your hand over it until life returns to its original place; and do so once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is good; and if not, if you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you must do in its chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you must cure it by medicines and this is of no use: therefore put the patient’s head in your hand; after that withdraw the cautery which will form later on in part as if you were putting on a bandage; and put in the cautery hot instantly, and keep your hand over it until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that withdraw your hand and repeat the cautery as you please; after that fill the patient’s mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and rinse out vigorously.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part therefore it remains moving if confirmed, and the joint softens restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
de la dolor des dens	And in part therefore it remains moving if confirmed, and the joint softens restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical remedies do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the burr and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If you take burr of ivy, and the end put in a spoon of iron or pewter; after take cotton and wrap over the point of a thread, and the soft tissue in burr, and put over the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cold; and do this often until the marrow comes out to the root of the tooth, and if you see if soft marrow and cotton in burr slip, and put over the aching tooth, and put over it a little iron that is hot until the heat comes to the cheek of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is thus: if you grasp a piece of iron or charcoal, and it is thick so that the fire does not reach the patient’s mouth; then burn the cautery, when it has formed, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cold; do this often, for the pain will be great of itself or the next day. And it is proper that the patient fill his mouth with saliva in the haste of this cautery, and then draw it out; this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do the cautery as you wish, and as you please; this is the form of the cautery.
des scrophules	of scrofula.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the lymph nodes are full of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not subject to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the fire cautery from the chest immediately, for otherwise there will be swelling. Make a small incision on the other side of the body and bring the cautery close to the wound once, or twice if necessary; and as soon as it reaches the root of the wound, if the wound is small, put the cautery on according to the size of the wound and leave it for two days; and put a soaked bandage over the wound until the pain is gone. Then cure the wound of its inflammation and pus until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When moisture overcomes the veins of the armpits and the face, and especially when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary to evacuate the patient first with solvent medicines; then make the cautery at the root of the throat, and keep it there until it reaches the throat, and do not go further than that. Then make another cautery at the junction of the collarbone and the spine, which is called the "clavicle," as we have seen; and cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed

de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement. dou cautere de pleuresin	of the pleura.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant. The cautery is not effective against hydrophobia, except in the manner called "asclytes." When you treat it according to the methods we have mentioned above, and your cure does not help, then you must give three cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, and two at the back on the spine, and one in the buttock; and let the cautery be very close to the root of the hair.

After leaving the cautery over for a long time to cool, do not leave the dressing on the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be reunited with the help of God.

de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the flesh.

de la menoison	After that, make two cauteries on the thigh at the point of the cubital angle; and let the cauteries be long, one above the knee and the other below, in the middle of the thigh; and leave the cauteries over a long distance in order to cure, that they may stay put; after that cure the other wounds that we have mentioned.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as the retentory and digestive virtue which is the stomach and the intestines is evacuated, and cannot be cured by methods of treatment; and you see the patient very suffering and of great distress, if you make a great cautery on the stomach as it has been said above or a cautery of the stomach, to the cautery that circulates; and three cauteries around the spleen at all three cauteries.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the navel and on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one; for the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	If you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the navel and on each side, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one; for the cure is beneficial when there is good assistance.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are deeply rooted, or several, and are old and are composed of thick, cold, and moist humors, they are cured as we have said in divisions; and it does no good to make cauteries: indeed, on the spine of the back, which is most painful to almsgive, and in triangulating, and on the buttocks; two must suffice.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you think the stomach is cold, the meat is raw, and the face is swollen, then the face should be cauterized with a great fire directly over the stomach, and another over the liver, and another over the spleen with all the nails of the forceps; and leave the fire on for a long time. After that, cure the wound until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	If you think the stomach is cold, the meat is raw, and the face is swollen, then the face should be cauterized with a great fire directly over the stomach, and another over the liver, and another over the spleen with all the nails of the forceps; and leave the fire on for a long time. After that, cure the wound until it is healed.
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you deal with the thelul [shoulder dislocation], if you see the cautery that appears to scrape away, then put it all alight on that thelul that is coping; and leave it until the vein is born again without support. de plaie mal curee	From an unhealed wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure the size or opening, as we have heard, if any ailment comes to pass that can only be cured by cautery
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If no fistula comes, and is filled with putrefying and moist pus, if the physician desires to perform an attempt, and maintains that you should soak it with all your might. Afterwards remove the cautery which appears to remove it, and insert it into the fistula as much as it is desired, and repeat the cautery until the flesh is stiff and corrupted; once, or twice, or thrice, according to the quantity of matter that is necessary; and take care of the nerves that are around it, and of the large veins. If the fistula goes up to the bladder or intestine, if you take care of these parts, do not do more than in the open air, and think that it will not go away; after that cure the part as much as it is sane, and if the parts are stiff and the matter is solidified, then soak that the part is completely healed; and if the matter is not solidified, soak that the part is flexible, and the os is corrupted by it; and thus as we have said above.
de la maladie des reins	Of the diseases of the kidneys.
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from the flanks comes with swelling and great windiness, and does not abate from a woman, then it is to be known that it must be cauterized on the flanks on one side and the other with the clamp cautery which we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize it in the middle, if there are two cauteries in a line, it will do more good.</start_of_turn>
de la vessie	Of the bladder.

de la marris	De la marris.
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	De la hainche.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moisture descends into the hip joint, and for this reason if it moves out of place, the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the knee is bowed outwards, so you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint at the circumference, and hold the limb steady around the joint as it rotates, until the joint is within the circle; and if it is cauterized like that which we have cauterized the stomach.

If these cauterizations are not sufficient, make two olive-sized cauterizations, and let them be as deep as all the others; and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the hip.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the groin, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of this by what we have said in the preceding section, and the cure is not of recent origin: therefore it is appropriate that you purge the patient of the gross humors with foul pills, or other solid pills that are similar.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the fire cautery is as follows: mixed medicines are burned, and fire cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: it is made in the shape of a triangle with good depth and breadth, and there is between each cautery a space equal to the thickness of two fingers; and the cautery should be olive oil. Never make the cautery in the middle of the shoulder, for there are three according to this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cautery is at the circumference of the shoulder that we have mentioned in the dislocation of the shoulder; but make part of the manner that the circumference contains the whole shoulder, and that all the edges of the circle are firm.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. And this is how it is done in sciatica, when the pain persists in the groin and does not reach the thigh or the leg. And if it comes as far as the thigh and the leg, the physician must make three cauteries there or the patient declares that the pain persists, and make a cautery below the ankle three times, one on the left side and two on the right; either the superficial cautery or the deeper cautery is to be used; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two toes or close to it, the area is to be cauterized at the point where the pain is felt, twice or thrice at the cautery which is called "the points."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the limb is stiff, if he does it more; and if he finds that the pain extends from the hip to the thigh, he makes a superficial or circular cautery there, and takes good care in all his cauteries not to burn the nerves and great arteries, and not to cause the patient more pain and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	I myself have seen many people who have cauterized the ankle bone of the foot, and left it until the leg was completely limp, and it bled profusely, and was perforated and corrupted throughout. After a solution of the belly from which death resulted.

de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back.
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from sitting or from percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things like cold spreading matter, of none of these signs is the cautery useful, for it is only for what comes from the infusion of cold matter
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after this that the patient be devoid of foul pills or other things, that one should make on his back, to the left or to the right where the pain persists, three lines marked with a needle, and in the center line three cauteries or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made according to the cautery which is called the "pointed" cautery. And if you see, make two or three cauteries at the middle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small child, and the signs of its approach are when it has twisted the skin around the joint when it happens, and fear; and you find behind the lower spine in the back and on the appearance that comes after the others.

de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when the pain originates in the heel, it is commonly called "podagre." When the cause is cold and the condition does not respond to medicines, it may be cured by cautery in a partial manner: make the mouth of the cautery enter the joint at the heel and use the cautery of olive oil in this form.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	When there is a need to prick the heel of the limb, if you perform the cautery over the entire area called "point," and if the pain extends to the knees and other joints and this occurs frequently, perform the cautery on each knee twice or thrice with olive oil; if further treatment is required, do so but do not hold your hand too tightly until the burn is over
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	If the pain descends to the knees and back, administer the cautery as described in the chapter. If the pain persists in the hands, prick around the wrist joint three lines; if there is no further pain in this area, prick on some joint and the root of the hand; if the pain extends to the buttocks or shoulders, cauterize some part and give the patient good instructions and medicines. For if you give them good instructions and evacuate phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	From the root of the scapula.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bones descend as coions, this is new; so if you see that it must be cured, do not move it immediately; and use things that leave the belly exposed, so that the pain descends from the belly; then make it sit on its buttocks between your hands, and command it to hold its shoulder tight until the bones are repaired, and hold it at your sides, and mark an indentation on the scapula above the elbow, and do all that is similar to half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery thus:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is soft and emits scents. Then bring the bones back to their place; and the minister holds his hand over that they do not return backwards; and take care well of the patient’s wounds, and put some cotton and some lint on the wounds, and another on the hand that holds them; then put the cautery on the mark at your whole hand, and keep it straight and hold it until you have touched the bone, and if you do not succeed the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware carefully that the bones do not protrude when you make the cautery; do not burn them; and by this means the patient will not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain. And it must be known that the cautery of children should be subtle in measure as the measure of the small people; and of the great people also great in measure; after two days the cure of the burn is completed as long as the swelling is bony; after that the cure of other ailments is completed when they are healed, and rest the patient forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and it must be known that his movements must be restrained for a long time, so that the swelling does not go out when he is about to walk in bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, he must be supported with a well-made cushion, and be carried for forty days; and let him rest well, that he work little and take little strong drink, and avoid eating too much; and when he has learned this, if he is healed entirely.
