But the first cauteries are lighter and more tender.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	There is no ancient pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain arises in any limb, whether from sitting or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with the cautery in accordance with the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its toughness and its twisting and its pain. If it is cured with the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery again. Indeed, it is customary that it must be burned towards the adjacent limb, for it is believed that in this way one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, whether from sitting or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, the remedy of medicine is not sufficient; therefore it is recommended that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with the cautery in accordance with the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its toughness and its twisting and its pain. If it is cured with the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery again. Indeed, it is customary that it must be burned towards the adjacent limb, for it is believed that in this way one can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The malady of the spleen is never aided by cautery in any way, and indeed the disease itself that comes from the corruption of humors and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, take note if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not linger, for you doubt that the corruption does not reach the whole ailment, so you make five cauteries on the head: that is, one on the top of the head, and one at the front of the ears to the end of the hair; and two on the two corners, and one behind the hair; and leave the hand as long as the cautery comes up to the bone, and as long as the membranes come out forcefully so that the vapors of the humors can escape; and cauterize the mouse according to what is before it.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	If mixed moisture is scattered everywhere; and it becomes apparent, if you command to cauterize from these cauteries which we have said or chief, namely cauterize once low down, and twice on the spine of the neck, three on the spine of the back, one great one on the armpit and one elsewhere, and twice on the two scapulae, twice on the flanks, twice on the tendons of the wrist and elbow, and once on any joint of the hands and feet, and on the sinuses of the hands; take care of the nerves which are on the back of the calcaneus, so that you do not burn them; and never make an incision on the bone of the eyebrow, or on the bone of the stomach, or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And as for the wounds, the more cauteries you make, the more aid you provide, and more benefit you yield; and as for the patients, they do not feel pain from the cautery as much as they would feel it if they were healthy, for the flesh is already corrupted. It is necessary that the cauteries be great and small according to the limbs and joints, as you would do in handling herbs. After treatment, cover the wound several times with flour and honey and other remedies until it is healed
de enfleure	and then of swelling.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not completely healed, then it must be cauterized on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either the cautery should be applied once in the middle of the swelling or several times at the edge. Then it must be dressed with ointment until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the site of a nerve that makes the limb immobile. And if it is a bony swelling, all these things must be known about the limb and the course of the moving nerves and bones.
de albaras	When swelling arises in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not completely healed, then it must be cauterized on the limb according to the size and degree of the swelling; and either the cautery should be applied once in the middle of the swelling or several times at the edge. Then it must be dressed with ointment until it is healed. And under no circumstances should cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the site of a nerve that makes the limb immobile. And if it is a bony swelling, all these things must be known about the limb and the course of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicines are of no avail, then it must be cauterized with a single burn, according to the amount of swelling in the area, until the swelling is hard and changes colour; then it must be dressed with flour from time to time, with rose oil and plantain leaves, with charcoal and alum, one part of each; and all these things must be mixed together, and bound with a bandage, and left in place until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre first begins, and you see it stop, if you cauterize with a circle-shaped cautery, all around the circumference of the chancre.  And all the wise men say that one should cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but I do not think that is good, because I fear that it will ulcerate and corrupt it, and I have already seen that happen several times; and the right thing is that it be cauterized around, with the circle-shaped cautery, as we have said concerning other cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati," and it lingers without dying out or by the excessive action which it makes or by the swelling of the patient when decrepit (that is to say too old) and there is much blood, or for fear; and you see that it hastens to die out: then cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it alone. For it will soon die out.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see that it is perishing throughout the entire cautery, if it is hot, make the cautery smaller; for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Put your hand in the middle of this ailment which is called "adubelati" while the cauteries have perceived the heat, and be such cauteries as the patient feels less pain in parts as they progress towards death. After that, cure until they are perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	The burn cautery. Another method of treating diseases is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than the swelling of a limb, because it causes the limb to swell as if by fire. If you see this disease in a patient who can endure fire cautery, then burn the nails small and great according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after which burn all the parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains but bone. And then leave it for two days, and put on the cauterized limbs and burn with oil until the burn wounds are ossified, and all the corruption is gone. After the cure of these wounds has lasted three days, if the swelling has not subsided, it is good; if it has not, repeat the burn on what remains swollen. This swelling has never been cured by medical treatment other than fire cautery; but every kind of fire cautery is of greater help, as I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	portions that come as pieces.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times it happens that when a piece of flesh comes out by itself a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing which boils up from the bowels. And the cautery of this disease is in two ways. That is to say, fire cautery and aquae calida. Fire cautery is when one is scorched like a pine twig, and is made of iron of the measure that it can penetrate all parts, and there must be subtle margins; after that one puts all around over the abscess, and holds the hand all around the abscess until it comes to the front of the abscess; and one leaves it thus for two days until it begins to secrete pus; then one makes an embolus of wild mallow bruised with oil, and leaves the embolus on all night, and closes the abscess tightly and will remove it from its root. Then cure the wound by wiping with char until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted by discharge of the abscess, and many times happen in hands and feet, if one must bring cautery of aquae calida; and in this part is the manner: take a needle of spider or iron, or a pine twig, and put on the abscess and the surrounding tissue, that is to say, prick the varices; and put the needle on so that it reaches all around, then put a little of hot oil, and hold the hand firmly, and press the hand by turning so that the margin of the needle reaches the root of the abscess, and can find the aquae calida going deep down to the root; and offer the patient a little of the aquae calida an hour; then leave it alone, and it will discharge all its roots. Thus do another, until you have extracted all that is in the abscess, then cure the wounds that arise from scratching with char.
li cure dou trembler	it cures trembling.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shiver from cold or from a quartan fever or from another, if you order them to undergo three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach just below the naval; if you leave them thus, they will stop shivering and the disease will be overcome.
des pustules puans	When some shiver from cold or from a quartan fever or from another, if you order them to undergo three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach just below the naval; if you leave them thus, they will stop shivering and the disease will be overcome.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Whenever pus comes to the surface, the body bathes, or there appear boils filled with pus, which come from corrupt matters. If you order it at the first sign that it appears, order a cautery on each head of the boil: a subtle cautery with a stick of myrrh, or with the tip grasped by the fire, or with long aristologe root, or with the lenticular cautery. And never burn them at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, for they do not advance further, but are broken by the superfluousness from which they come, and are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	When the artery is cut, there are often great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a mournful thing to extend it.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens, if you are quick to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and hold it tight without being appeased by the blood, and does not bleed any more; then take again the olive cautery, large or small as you please, and when they are all red; then take hold of the thumb or great toe as much as is necessary so that the artery is not obstructed, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery until it is fixed.</start_of_turn
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out fiercely when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take hold of another cautery that is in the fire immediately.</start_of_turn
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do this one after the other until the limb is stretched out; keep guard that you do not touch the nerve which is below, and that no other mischief comes upon the patient; and take care that when the artery is large, it is not properly filled even with the best treatment, except in three ways: by cautery, or by extraction if it is not otherwise treated, or by strong stitching with thread, or by medicines placed on which have power to fill the blood.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about a rest of the limb by tightly draping it or by putting on hot things upon it, or other similar things, if this does not prove helpful in no way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is no remedy and no medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it firm until it is healed from the wound and from the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it often with cold water so that it should be cold as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and healed; and do poultices in front of that which he must cauterize and medicate
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This sentence translates as:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have already said in the first chapter that every disease in which it is appropriate to use fire cautery, or burning medicine, we shall consider the incisions, the causes, the instruments, and the forms of cautery; and in this chapter we shall treat the chief diseases from the head downwards, and I shall speak of them by the same way as before because we have found it to be lighter in this way.</start_of_turn>
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, I must tell you, dear sir, that there is more danger and fear in this chapter than in all the previous cautery, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you must not be rash. For many people come to cures in such a way that if they do not succeed in their ailment, they become lighter from their disease and from the greatness of their malice; and of these things we must be wary.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are those who make sense and say: "Wait, I am a liar"; and the ailment is grievous. It befits me only that you allow those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not trust me foolishly but wisely of that of which you are certain, and of which you have taken and learned; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation is either converted or preserved; and that will help you to ask for good fame, glory, and memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our lords, you must understand and be skilled, and if you turn to the inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordonné ce chapitre en divisant par Chapitre, selon ce qu’il est devant ou Chapitre des cauteries, que j’vous ai devisé de chef jusques à pied, pour ce qu’il vous trouve plus facilement ce qu’il vous avez mérité.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded you this chapter by dividing into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have commanded from head to foot, because it will be easier for you to find what you have desired.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Saiches that this disease comes from time to time with great swelling of the head of the child; and when the swelling is too great, the head of the child is strained.  Never comes this from any other cause than that it is not set right.</start_of_turn>
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen such a disease leave so quickly as in the summer; and with all that I have heard, it seems to me that it is better to leave the work in parts rather than to cure it all at once.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood when the shoulder was dislocated, the head grew so large that it could not be sustained; and it was believed that the moisture was so great that it became a tumor, and when this moisture is gathered between the bones above the scapula, between the humerus and the scapula, and the work is such that if the moisture is between the humerus and the scapula, and the incision is made too small, you must make a wide incision; and be as long as necessary, until the moisture has gone.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, if you make two incisions like a cross, following this form:

Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez. For the fire cautery is useful for extracting arteries that are filled with much fat and putting on strong stitches; and when you remove them, if there is no cure for dry medicines that make new flesh grow, and strong stitches, until they are healed; and if you do not take care of the artery as much as you should, if you hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use vinegar in your hand that is not stained; and if you do not have this present, if you must remove the vein you must do so while it is still warm, and rise the cold water until it stops bleeding, and strain as much as you can; and what is more numb and lighter in the extraction of the artery is to cauterize the vein for a third of its length, but the cautery should be well spaced to prevent it from staying too long.

Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they call it the ancient "cure contuse." de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is seen in the ears is one of three things: grains, or pus, or stone or like iron; or seed, as in grapes, beans, peas; or a flowing substance as in wound and boils and like things.</start_of_turn>
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a stone or other foreign body in the ear that does not fit inside the ear, do not put the ear down. If you see a stone, if there is no discharge of violet oil or sesame oil, then do not delay treatment; and loosen the earwax. Make the patient cough up mucus, and stop the bleeding by placing pieces of cloth or wool around the ear. Keep the ear raised.</start_of_turn
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	When it bursts out with these bites, it is good; if this does not happen, do an incision with a fine needle; and if it does not burst with this, take a piece of gut and put some cotton around it, and press on the swelling above the gut as much as it will go without causing harm, and bring out the swelling.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	When the ear is acutely inflamed, then the patient must immediately apply a compress to the ear and fill it with wool. And if the inflammation is on the same side as the ear, or if it is on the other side and the ear jumps for this reason, that is good. If not, take many pills as the length of your finger requires to hold and support them, and push them into the fire; and put the patient one or two fingers into the ear, and pull out from the other side, and push with another finger against the finger which is in the ear; and do this until the inflammation is entirely gone. If you see that it is not diminishing, take a piece of sponge and hold one of the bones in the ear, and the other bone press with fire as long as the pain persists; then do the same with the other bone until the inflammation is entirely gone, as we have said concerning the finger.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small size, as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great size, it can be felt, so you must perform an extraction of wisdom teeth; and this is the easiest thing to do in the ear.

Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. And if they do not obey to withdraw, if I grasp the edge of the cotton ball as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, give distillations that the ancients have proved useful in the incision of worms, and you shall find them or treat them with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, thus is the form as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let the silver or gold be thoroughly loosened from the bottom to the top, with a few slight tears, and from above over the distiller; and press with a well-made instrument of gold for this purpose. If you see take a scraper and wrap around the tip immediately cotton; then pour in your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines in the cannel, and the cannel be in the ear; then press back into the scraper with all the cotton, and press your hand steadily until the oil is distilled or almost all the way from the ear; and let the patient feel within, and let the distillations be no more smoky than when they are distilled in the ear; and keep that they are not too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding the ear swelling,
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a mark upon their ear; and the same thing happens as with wounds or a burst ear drum in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see them; and never is there any trace of having had a burst.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	No child is born without a mark upon their ear; and the same thing happens as with wounds or a burst ear drum in the ear, for these bursts never happen without leaving a mark on the ear, if one does not see them; and never is there any trace of having had a burst.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it that it is seen and known before and behind all around, if it does not bleed the ear; if the bursting is of a burst ear drum or a swelling of the ear, if you have subtle pinches, and hold it lightly, as long as that burst is entirely bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the ear opening is plugged by a foreign body, take a fine needle and scoop out a small piece of the earwax with fire; then place the foreign body out of the ear. If you feel the foreign body that the patient feels in the ear, pierce lightly and do not damage the nerves of the ear; then insert a plug of cottonwool into the ear, according to the size of the hole.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not do anything until the wound is healed; then take a sponge and soak it in rose-water, sprinkle with powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swelling, it is likely that you must remove the plug and apply another sponge soaked in oil of roses and beeswax until the swelling subsides.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	If blood vessels swell, immerse a sponge and wring it out in cold water, place it on the ear, and apply other treatments that are useful for stopping blood flow which is causing the swelling.
de la char des papieres	De la char des papiers.

From the stack of papers comes this treatise which comes from the blood of the eyes when they are moist and dry, if you stretch them out with nails and pinches, and grasp the root with a spatula; then extract the glassy vitriol that is bruised.

de la gresle	From the grease.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in papers the tears of things that seem to groan in their form and in their hardness; for this is the disease called "granulin," and is an assembly of great moisture in the belly and in the bowels. The work is like this: take warning when the granulin moves from one side to the other; and it is a light thing to know. Then make a large incision, then burn the fatty part lightly, then take hold of the tweezers, and pull. If you do not grasp it in the right direction, the belly will grieve nothing to the patient; and if the tear is great, if the assembly has a costure, and cure until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make force, for it will restore itself quickly and cause no harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granulin descends into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the belly, and pull out the granulin with tweezers, pressing from one side and the other; and if the belly is stripped by the incision, this will grieve nothing; and when the granulin is pulled out, if you leave the dirty oil, cure the belly of that which causes harm until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the tears
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is enclosed in paper tissues, and this happens more with women than with men, and grieves moist at their eyes, and they come out with tears in the mornings, and cannot look at the sunlight because the tears hurry away from their eyes; and because of this they sleep with their faces down, and their papers are soaked with their tears which swell and appear covered in exinach which comes out in oil. And when you press their hand to their armpits and feel the exinach between their arms.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	If the patient puts their head in their right place; and then take one towel of linen, and make a loop resembling a circle according to the quantity of exinach from the armpits, and put it on; and press on the two sides, so that the exinach is assembled like the circle; then make half of the moisture at the tip of the knife cutting a wound not greater than the wound made to the vein; and make the skin taut as long as you see the exinach; and in many situations comes out exinach from the wound, according to the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out the bones at all a blunt piece of marrow between your arms to the side, and twist your hand to the right and to the left as much as it is sparse; and keep that you do not join in the wound, that you do not live until all the marrow is out, that you do not bruise it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it emerges not at the commencement of the wound, if you expand a little the wound slightly until it opens; then remove it as we have said, and moisten the edges with oil and water, and place over it, and strain of bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who bite their tongues and put over them to corrupt the moisture that is gone. Then cure until it is healed. And if it comes to the vein above the wound, if you cure the abscess gently as much as possible.</start_of_turn>
des poilz des papieres	paper hair
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers are born with hairs attached other than their natural state, and are enclosed, if they irritate the eyes, they cause various diseases like tears which are usually excessive and softening of papers and gum, as much as this is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by water-based medicine as it is before or alongside fire cautery, or by incision and suture or by ligature, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, and move the paper from your right hand; if it is converted, that is good; if not, if there is a splinter of any size through all the thread below; either cut off the margin of the paper or the hairs will be cut off; and take out one thread from below at all the paper, and move it to the top; then make on the lower part of the paper, below the hairs, below all the fat up to the big tear, and pull out one thread, and put under the paper a small piece of cotton and bandage, and sign on the paper a figure like a nutmeg, and it must be so that the figure is according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is devised to you.

et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And never has it happened that the hair of the beard has been converted: if you use what we have said concerning incision; but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard hair and the surrounding area as we have said, then make three incisions by art, and three threads as long as the beard and expand in a circle; and take three hairs from three parts or hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other securely over what rests on the beard oil, and strain the three boils from the three parts forming; and leave it for a few days, and the skin that has been strained will swell and darken and become black, until it disappears by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the boil has increased in force, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has healed, and when the beard has fallen out, the hair will not grow again; and this is the form of the three boils that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil. Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase at the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out from under and you see it through the sight of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread and close the oil and leave it closed for a quarter or two days, until the hair has returned to its place and the burden is gone.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or putrefaction comes to light, if there are two methods: one natural, and the other unnatural.  And it arises from a wound, or from a cut or cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way of working on this is that you make that suture, and dry the flesh, and put in there some linen threads, and leave it until it is healed; and do not do anything but use in the treatment of this things that dry and restrain. For if you do that, if the disease comes back worse than before; but there are things that soften, such as fennel; and alum or salt and mustard seed boiled in oil, and it covers a bandage, and it cures this.</start_of_turn>
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in a different form than it had before; for this work that we have said is not fierce except in addressing this disease, that it does not return in a different form than before.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the burn that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	From the burn that comes in oil, this disease which is truly called "axacrati", is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and fracture and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in this case is that if you take an awl, because it has two threads, and the thread is in the burn, and it makes the left armpit bleed so much that the thread is split in two at the elbows of the burn; then the burn is taken out from under the awl, and the wound has one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound returns in the same way as it is supposed to, that is good; but if not, take one scraper and put it into the fracture, and twist the wound, and make two incisions or break two ribs inside the wound; and if there are two incisions of two angles of the incision that you have made, or make an angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the letter that has not "j. grieche"; then break that burn, according to the quantity of its ribs and its burn, of what that teaches the wound, then join the two ends that are loosened, and bind with a thread of linen; then cure this according to what we have said of the mollifying medicines and compresses, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a fracture or a sprain or a cautery, if you must make a full incision along the hairs of paper, as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons know best how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him in more diverse circumstances.
dou soudement de la papiere	And if the disease comes from a fracture or a sprain or a cautery, if you must make a full incision along the hairs of paper, as above; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the surgeons know best how to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is convenient for him in more diverse circumstances.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this swelling has happened at home in a part like this that the paper beneath is solidified with oil, and cannot move or do its natural work, if you must drink the point of a scraper from the paper, and hold it up; and extend as little as possible, as long as you can tolerate what is airy in the swelling, which must not be too much and not too little, for the patient must not suffer too much from the swelling and must not burn the oil; and for your incision, which you should carefully drain, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all that is assembled should be healed, and do not make any more cuts in the oily water, and lift the water soft and clear, and some vinegar; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put on the oil wool loosely in abundance; and after that use oil of meadowsweet and other things soothing as long as it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the root of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nails of the oil are of two kinds: one is nervous and similar to hard pitch, and the other is not nervous but is similar to white moisture congealed. When one touches them with fire and boils them with oil, they do not burn; and both appear to swell towards the greater marrow, spreading throughout the whole eye and the light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to make the incision is as follows: if the patient places his head in a healthy position, then he opens the eye; and the physician holds the eyelid with his hand, then he cuts the nail with small double-edged scissors, and stretches it downwards; then he takes a needle, and puts in one hair of a horse, or of a calf, or of a bull, and one strong thread; and he doubles the point of the needle a little and fixes it into the nail, and pierces it through with the needle, and ties the nail with a thread and stretches it downwards, and washes all around the nail the costae of the nail which surrounds the nail-root and the hair to the hair, and leaves the natural moisture or the tear, if there is no occasion for tears to come out usually; and in no case does the nail retract only by the incision, and by the thread, as we have said; then he washes away all the surrounding fat with the sponge. This is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the fatty tissue and breaks it, and that the needle does not pierce through; and after the incision pour oil into the wound a little bit of burnt salve, and give some lard, and leave it until the other side; then cure what has come to pass until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push the needle, and the thread cannot enter, many times it is cured of this semblance of a nail of medicine; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you cover the oil of the patient, and take the sponge lightly somewhat like this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And withdraw the nail gradually, and if you see that it has diminished somewhat and the flesh has pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil lard, make lard and red salve and burnt salve, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work according to this same work, until it is entirely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders you, if like an incision, if necessary, hold the milk and cure the wound first until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.

If there appears fat in the oil during the night, if it is fat that is soft and not thick, that is not fat; then distil in the red oil of poppyseed, which is made from litharge.</start_of_turn>
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the seed that grows on the plum tree.
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyes of some men never burst once; cover the navel and restrain the papers and burn them to the ground, and it seems like a rosebud; and if the patient places his head in his stomach, then do the eyes, and all that hair has a convenient length for this, and the support is strong; then grasp the first hair, and go on grasping until the end, and keep only two drops of oil during the work. et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance. des voines des eulz	des voines des eulz
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	Red veins covered with fat, endure the sight of an eye and make the fat swell all the days. The physician must first look at the eye to see if the fat is soft or hard; there is no other disease more violent than this; therefore, the physician must do this part carefully: instruct the patient to put his head in his hand, then suspend the veins throughout their length as he deems appropriate, and let the physician double the ligature as much as he deems necessary:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then suspend the veins throughout their length as he deems appropriate, and let the physician double the ligature as much as he deems necessary:

Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers. puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide. de l’issue de l’oil	Then put your thumb on the bone below the armpit, withdraw your hand from the oil quickly, pull the whole limb until it breaks the bone and the patient feels it through that which comes into being if he holds his hand on his elbow; and then restore the dry limb, as I have taught you, and when the wound has healed and the limb has become firm, if there is still something to be done for the elbow; if it is less burdensome for the patient.

de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
