Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a little rest, when the water returns for the second time, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly secured and does not rise, grasp the almagda lightly by wrapping your hand around it and around; then put back into the water a little of the remnant of the salve. Then put upon the wound some soaked linen or cotton soaked in oil of roses and plenty of eggs, and tie with the healthy oil.  Thus, and those who are with us of our party, put on above the wound some soft material with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil because there are parts of bone that have too hard the veins, it is to be known that you take the instrument which is called “alberit,” which is like this in shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctive alone, and do not wander too much around, but make a small incision, then insert the ligature, as we have said; and when the work is finished, appears to the patient a certain slumbering arising, in which he sleeps on his back for one gloomy night; and do not allow any movement, and take nourishing food, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and bind it as he wishes until three days; then take it out of this house and let him see, and make him see whatever he wants to see, and then put it back in until the seventh day; and do not let him do anything else except for this treatment or after the incision now, but make sure you feed him, for the pain will mount excessively.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And thus when the swelling subsides, take away the oil before the seventh day, and bring it to that which alleviates the abscess; and when it is calmed, take out the ligature and put on his face a little cushion to cover any hair; and keep it in this gloomy house. And then go out of the house and go home, and let it be as it wishes; and let no disciple interfere in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some came to us from the Yrach who said that in their peace they had seen a man bite his tongue when the water was successful, but we have never seen or read of such a thing in our land or in the books of the ancients; and by chance it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the signs of the forms of an almond, for those who do not know them; and they are like pearls properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their tops are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like a hook.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	of the seed from the nut
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes new or old hairs appear various, as if scorpions had teeth; and if there are such or if there is hair entangled with lice of a black color, or if there is hair of a pale bone color. In those in which these hairs are pale, and do not entangle, it is enough to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and cover his nose, and spit on those hairs, and push them away; then take what you have in hand to support under the thumb of a part, until you are certain that that hair is completely dry.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If nothing remains to hold it, if the wound has all its edges loose, if nothing remains to keep it; if it does not settle, or if it is proud, or if there is an abscess, or if there are sharp objects in it, or if it is malignant, then hasten and cauterize as much as possible until all the edges are bound and fixed; then drain or remove the pus easily and quickly, or vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the swelling does not subside, and moisture comes up to the palate, the stitches that held it together are now useless; if moisture does not yield as it should, the swelling that was above the bone now appears under the skin; accordingly, do not try to pull out the instruments by force: just as before, pull out the thread a little at a time, and tie a knot at the root of the thread between each stitch, so that there is neither too much nor too little space between them; and put the patient’s hand over the thread at the root of the stitches and hold it down firmly with the other hand, and catch one after the other as they rise up from the root towards the mouth; and do this until the child has spat out all the teeth, as it is a light matter for one who has seen it done; then keep the chief that comes from the root at one hand, and the other chief that comes from the mouth at the other hand, and catch the one after the other as they rise up holding both hands, until you have caught up all the teeth that were left in the socket; do this until you have caught all the roots that remain in the swelling. Then take out the thread, dry the wound, wet the thread again in Egyptian balsam, and reinsert it as before; do this for two or more days, until the swelling has dissolved all the remaining root matter. Then put in or remove a plug of wool until the wound is healed, and if necessary use drying medications; this is the form of the instrument for purging the chief, from which the oils and medications are distilled or not.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Be it silver or gold, resembling an overblown lamp, if like a cord; if you see it, make a closed loop, and keep the instrument flat to purge the chief; and have one hand on the chief to hold it when pouring oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the head of the neck a disease which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes very great indeed, so that it is seen; and for this reason it is necessary that you should immediately take hold of the beginning and break the bone, then put out the fire or the burning medicine; and if you delay in taking hold of it when it is great, if you do not take hold of it firmly, of a pale color, of little sense: if you do not touch it with iron, for it is a burnt abscess, for when you take hold of it once, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of pale color, and you see that you can take hold of it completely, if you see the patient vomiting and taking hold in vain, cure the limb of dry things and restraints.</start_of_turn>
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Wounds that, when the healing process advances, reach one of these painful cartilages, indeed yield to the advantage of some. It is therefore prudent that this should not be the case with any wound, for if the patient perceives the wound to be fresh throughout its entirety, then he should join the two layers of skin at a costure and cure it until it is healed; and if the layers have already separated from one another, then he should carefully support all the surrounding parts until they bleed again, then reunite the two layers of skin at a costure, and strain them, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood over them; and burn incense. And place upon the powders a piece of thick or other closing dressing. Leave it until it discharges by itself, and cure it until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is as follows: or by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	from the armpits of the arms.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home in the hands, there are from the thumbs to the little finger, some that are like grains of wheat, smaller and greater; thus it is that you must break the nails, make incisions at the base of each nail, and grasp them with tweezers and press them into the flesh; then employ the lancet after the incision of the carbuncle, until it is not stained; and then remove it easily, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the heel of the jaw.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it happens on the gums that a tumor appears, which they formerly called "albules"; if you support it, grasp the root and leave the socket or the blood out; then put out the lancet or other astringent and desiccant powders; and if the tumor comes back after the incision, and happens often, if you grasp it a second time, cauterize it: if it does not come back after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Whenever they are joined at the head of the tooth, between the gums, teeth that are loose and rough; never are the teeth black and yellowed towards, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if it is thought that one should make the patient sit between the hands, and that his shoulders are relaxed, and open the jaws or the teeth will burst open, until nothing remains; and then one makes black and green, yellow and other stains, as long as they are softened; and if one has seen this at the first attempt, it is well done; if this is not the case, one must repeat the second and third time, until everything is recovered; and the teeth that have been mentioned above have various forms of stripes, according to what the master of the work shows, for the raisers of teeth which one must drive out have other forms than those which one must drive between the teeth; and these stripes and others are seen with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you stay close to it for a while, because it must not be left alone; for it is a high-quality matter, therefore we have no excuse for neglecting it
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is constrained to do something, if you are certain that he will do it, many times he will suffer pain. Take care that the pain is neither too great nor too small, and make him do the thing which he must do; and whatever he does not do for this reason, as long as the illness persists, for we have already done it for these scoundrels; and when you are well certain that he will do it, if you push his hand strongly to the front of his tooth, then put the thumb and index finger of your hand firmly into the first and second phalanxes, and hold them firmly; and keep the patient's arm firmly in your hand between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After that, stretch the tooth directly towards the brisier; and if it does not move, take no instruments and hold the tooth loosely from the front; and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is seen to be loose and moving, if you can, cover it with gauze, or take it out; and if the tension is made too tight, that it does not break from the tension; and you must moisten around the tooth with saliva to soften it.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care well that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with the greatest pain of the first. And take care that you do not do anything that the ignorant physicians do, who break bones without any reason and do not bring any benefit, but only bring harm; but they bring no healing for the great disease that remains from the roots, or for the fracture that they break, as we have often wanted; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is bleeding, let us employ the powder of vitriol; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of instruments, since they must remain silent at first, whether with long points and broad handles, must not double in number when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root comes loose when drawing, if you must put out the moist cotton wool inside [i.e. toward the inside], as long as it is flexible; and then put back the forceps which are called “algefri,” so that the bone appears to be like a beak; and be made as with a file and that is the form:</start_of_turn>
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not yield to all these tensions, if you can, uncover the bark entirely around the root, and put the instrument which is called the «althali», which is to say a palanche, because of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it breaks not, and the root comes out by this, that is good; if not, if you aid it with all your tools, because the shapes will come after.</start_of_turn>
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has just rain, because of this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Or other instruments which precede the teeth, and of this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Or else great and firm to hold the bone, that it does not slip, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, if the disease has all of these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear contrary to their natural position, and their form is deformed, even in women of childbearing age, if it is suspected that they are deeply embedded and cannot be extracted without damage, then extract them entirely; and if they are embedded with the tooth, grasp this instrument which has a similar shape to a small beak, and which is made of iron without a jagged edge.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	When the tooth persists too long in the gums and in the hands, for the duration of the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file that has the same shape as the tooth
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	When the tooth persists too long in the gums and in the hands, for the duration of the tooth's hardness, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file that has the same shape as the tooth. And it is just like filing nails; and while you are filing the tooth slightly, so that it does not move too much, if it blanches, the tongue will bleed excessively, so if you want to avoid this, file the sharp edges until they are even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen, whether by percussion or biting, and the patient is unable to press on what hurts them, you must cure them with restrictive medicines, but this is not enough; if you command them to restrain themselves with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and is harmful, but the gum does not move at all; and whether the thread is thick or thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are aligned, if you take hold of the thread and double it between the two front teeth, then put the teeth between the other teeth, as many as there are, until you see it clearly up to the next tooth; then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and clearly, until it does not move; and whether your thread is loose at the root of the tooth if it cannot escape. Then close the teeth with the thread at a clasp, and assemble them, and put them back between the teeth, and put them in place so that they do not touch the tongue; and then leave them in place as tightly as they can stay in place, and if they slip or the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread; if it remains calm and useful for all its tension, and that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the front teeth and the back teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing interfere that is not wise and soothing, and never make its shape like a tooth of ivory, and put it back in its place where the fault is, and strain it as we have said, and hold and use it for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	The tongue is sometimes loosened from its socket by the swelling of the tongue or by nature itself; or by an accidental wound; the work is such that you must support the mouth of the patient, and hold his tongue, and then grasp the large nerve of the tongue, until the tongue is freed from its abode; and if there is any delay or if it be prolonged, and if it be from an injury, if you touch the artery which is loosened; and when you have done that, if you lift the pale or cold liquid, and put down the tongue a little, and hold the patient’s hand, that he cannot move it. And if blood comes from the wound, if you take out the broken glass; if it does not go away, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; and then you treat with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a black or brown or hard bubble, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a carbuncle; and if it is declining with moisture, if there is blood, if you touch the wound, and you make a splatter of blood, and deliver from a part and from another; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put on broken glass until it is stained, then return to your work until you have finished everything; then lift the pale liquid and the like, and treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	There are often abscesses in the throat that are called "godath," and they are usually full of pus, and when you treat them, as we have said previously, if they are not cured, take care: if these are hard abscesses of little size and with yellow pus, do not touch them with iron. And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron either, for fear of bleeding; but leave them as they are until they are dead, and then you can remove them, or they will burst by themselves; and if they are white in color and the root is slender, if you have brought the instrument to cover them, but first look to see if the abscess is settled and calm. Then make the patient sit in the sunlight, with their shoulders relaxed, and hold the mouth open and grasp the beard between their hands, and press the tongue downwards towards the instrument, as it is with a spoon; and let it be of silver or gold, or like a nail:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... and if you see the abscess, take the sponge and wipe it in the abscess, and push it down further than you think; and do not put anything of the towels on it, then close the instrument over the abscess, as it is with a spoon; and all the while the patient’s shoulders are bent, one place over the other, and are very sore, and is made of iron or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with pincers, know that this is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	If you do not have this instrument present, if you can manage with pincers, know that this is the shape:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I medicated a woman who had an abscess in her throat, which was so severe that she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had persisted in this state for even a day or two. The abscess was so high that it had forced its way out through two holes in the side of her throat. I then immediately applied some ointment to one of the holes, and when I had finished, I forced out a great amount of pus; then I repeated the process on the other hole in the side of her throat, and I closed her mouth and pressed her tongue; and when I had applied the ointment to these abscesses, and had closed one of them, only a little blood escaped from the other. I then removed the obstruction from her throat, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and she continued to vomit violently for a long time; and the abscess reappeared in exactly the same place as before, filling her body with fluid, until it became very large. Then I bound her and cauterized the abscess inside her throat: the abscess went away once more; and I left her with these parts removed, and only God knows what happened to her after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	From the navel.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there must be a lock of hair or something put over the medicine, as with the nails of a sickle; and put the instrument over all the medicine on the navel; and the patient must be sitting on his side, so that the saliva and mucus come out of his mouth from the medicine inwards, if it does not go down to the throat, and the sneezing; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the navel, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it turn pale and the biting of the medicine is appeased; and if you see that, take hold and cover it with any instrument, and moisten the cloth with the medicine, and withdraw the instrument from all around the cotton in the navel, until the cotton has dried over the navel; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it dry and wipe away after three or five days. And if you must restart the medicine, if you restart it, and after the cautery wipe the surrounding area with cotton wool soaked in vinegar, and bandage what is around the medicine; and be raised from cold water, and be cured of hiccups until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this method. Take camomile, rue, origanum, ivy, and chamomile, and assemble all or some of them in a pot. Put some oil in it and boil. The pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot is one instrument that should be fixed according to this method.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it may be of silver or lead, or one of the above-mentioned things be put into the patient’s mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the pain, until the eye is dead; and then the process is repeated frequently, until the eye is dry, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the swelling, for many things happen at that time; and do not do this except when the swelling subsides. And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and put inside the head of the egg a sliver of egg, so that the patient does not have too much pain; for the sliver of egg does not make the vapor hinder the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened at the throat bone or fish spine, or nothing at all; so it is necessary therefore that you prove what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, you must make the patient vomit the patient immediately when the meat is cooked in the stomach; even if it is expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and attach the sponge to a thread and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is expelled, then draw it out again; and if it does not come out by itself, take a sponge according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the curved instrument rest at the head if it can more easily enter through the throat, and keep the head raised; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for this can cause them to choke, do not push the bone inwards; and move quickly that the patient may hold the instrument, for if it slips or the thing is loose, since it has slipped down, or if it is forced too far, it will be equally broken.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the curved instrument rest at the head if it can more easily enter through the throat, and keep the head raised; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for this can cause them to choke, do not push the bone inwards; and move quickly that the patient may hold the instrument, for if it slips or the thing is loose, since it has slipped down, or if it is forced too far, it will be equally broken.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And never is medicine useless, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient’s tongue to the instrument I have mentioned. And if you see the tongue, if it has been pressed too far with the instrument that I have told you of. And if you see that the tongue has slipped, if there are small teeth or subtle tremors that are worth that. And if this is not worth it, take a spoonful of wine and put it in the patient’s throat, and then withdraw or bite the wine. And if the patient feels pain throughout, take a full look at cold water, cover the mouth and the vomit in the direction of swallowing, and move the tongue frequently; and if the patient feels the pain again, spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	If it does not prick at its base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is like this: it looks like a pair of pliers with teeth to enter the throat; and it looks like a beak of a heron, and there is a roughness of lime, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go. And when you have this shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the physicians of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	The wounds of incisions are, as it is remembered from one place to another in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two manners in which they occur. One is in their own image, and that which holds moisture. And the second manner is when they lie on bones or are at the joints. For the incisions on the head are other than those on the foundation, and the incisions on the forearm are other than those which occur at the joints, and the like has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If incisions are not perceived, as long as the bone is dead according to its course; and if there are some which must be perceived when they are callous, and do not die according to their course, like incisions which are from joints. For when incisions come from joints, and it is left as long as it is rigid, by chance if the tendon and nerve of the joint are ruptured, because of the contraction in that limb. Or the incision is from the principal limb, and if you wait until it is measured, if it is still there, if the limb is from the principle; or it is from the foundation, if the perforation is not yet dead. And you must only perceive a callous incision with digestion accompanied, except for that which is from the foundation, which must not be perforated, and must be prolonged, and there will be fistula; and it will not heal in a great length of time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	You must save the wound from the perforation of the incision which is dead according to its course; and when the pain is calmed, the departure of fever, the disappearance of pain and redness, the debate and the tingling of the head of the incision, and other signs; and you must make the perforation or more dependent on the wound, and the place where it opened wide; and either the perforation is long enough of the bone, and if the incision is at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and all the limbs are equal or there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier. dou chancre	And draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the cause of it, and bandage the limb.

Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	When the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the hydrosis is joined to the intestines: if it is that you must make an incision two fingers’ breadth to the right of the navel; and if the hydrosis is from the disease of the liver, it must be made to the left of the navel; and if it is from the spleen, it must be made to the right, and do not make it wider than necessary for the patient lies on the incision that the surplus blood does not flow to that weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce all the leather with the instrument, and the gut, and keep your hand over the whole area between the leather and the sac just as when escorting the amount of an nail or as thick as an almond; then pierce the sac until the area of the gut comes out, and that is the cause of the pain, then take out the instrument, and there you have the form: And it is similar to a silver nail, and is of flax or flaxseed, and has at the end a small hole; or it costs one part, two holes, and three on one side, and three on the other side, and the nail is cut as if with a penknife, and that is the shape of the incision which the writer makes with the penknife.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top of this is the alemele, so that when the instruments come to the pain, if you now put your hand on the instruments; empty out then half or a third part, for if you empty out more than that which is convenient in this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he cuts his palm, or he approaches death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But seeing the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the indications of the virtue tell the patient, and his pains; then take the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the thumb which is stamping the part which is above the socket, as I have said; pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering this, and take out a small quantity of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. de l’estopement de la verge	of the stomach of the thigh.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Never are children born without a birthmark on the verge, or the birthmark is small, or it is not in its proper place. If the midwife should doubt that there is no mark at all, despite searching very thoroughly according to this form: then she must make or discover a mark, that is, a mole of pitch, and bind it and hold it for two or three days. And when she wishes to urinate, if she keeps the mole closed, she will urinate, and then release it; and in this way it will not be closed, because the urine which comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the birthmark is small, if it is treated with a pitch mole, as we have said, if it expands. Those who do not have a birthmark in its proper place are blemished, for no one is born with a birthmark on the top of the verge, because they cannot urinate before they lift up their verge; and they cannot urinate backwards because the matter cannot come down to the marrow, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that if the patient lies groaning on his back, with the head of the verge and the buttocks as wide as a thumb, if the birthmark pricks in the middle, as it should; and you hold back the discharge of blood which comes many times, and if there is any, if you see the stain of that which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these boils appear in the groin, and are a sign of foul matter; and in them are both malignant and benign; if you take them away immediately, that is, with an ointment, and cut and drain them all out, then apply a wet compress in Egyptian fashion; then bind the wound tightly until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	If blood comes from a wound, if the lunar cautery is to be used in this fashion: The cautery helps in these three things together: that is, at the discharge of blood, and the corruption; and if the head of the bone is corrupted and withdrawn, if you bite or bring forth from the bone a bundle of hair, and make the patient urinate among them; and when the hair has reached the top of the bone which has not been circumcised, or if there is wound or incision, if you must therefore singe the bone with a sharp instrument until the ligaments are loosened and the bone is freed from all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	If this be a serious matter, if you must indeed singe the bone with a blunt instrument without causing further damage to the head of the bone and the skin; then smear gently between them, and put upon them a soft bandage of wet linen, slightly damp.
de la circoncision	with circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will, and do it with care, if we are able to make the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision in their laws, because they did not use it in their customs, and we have only what we have learned through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision with skill, force, and all their skill; but if the patient flees because of two or three towels, and by chance if one removes this one and leaves that one behind.

Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.

Or the wound covers again, and the pain is doubled, and at the movement which is done with too much force at the point of the limb; and at the movement of the tendon by chance escapes the iron, and repairs the work, and many times the nails are born again without having to make another incision, and I want that.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, if it is held equally from all sides in this way; but that the thread should be well stretched around the leather; and that the movement of the first work should be as if you were to make the child think, if he understands, that you do not force him to bind the thread around the limb too tightly, but rather let him be able to do it in all the ways that he can.</start_of_turn

The wound of the mundane if it is when the spur of the abscess bursts at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend your nail, even though it makes an incision; and hold it equally, and if you do not manage to hold your nail, if you keep holding, and then hold it.

dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine

et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer an extraction with all the instruments which are called a "siringue"; and this is formed as follows: either of hammered silver legier melted, like the quill of a bird; or of caine from the root of a long stem, or of silver at the head.</start_of_turn

puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then put the syringe into the bladder, until it reaches the root of the bladder; then double the bladder downwards towards the pelvis; then drain the syringe until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel the urine come until it is empty; this must not be done except in this order because it is harmful; then draw out the thread at the whole of the wool and at the end, the urine follows the wool, and it is driven out forcefully, and correct the urine
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the syringe until the bladder is empty, and align the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are flank stones or blood in the bladder, or if there is swelling, and you see urine and medicines being distilled, if you have at your disposal the instrument called the «clepsedre», which is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and if it is pierced: half from one side, and a third from the other, as you see; and you must hold the urine bag so that the medicine is as strong as possible and can compress the moisture, and push as much as necessary.
