de la piere	Of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the methods of dealing with stones, and their extraction along with medicines; and we have mentioned the difference between a stone that is incarcerated like a rain, and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be opened by size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney; and I will tell you openly and briefly.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is incarcerated in the bladder often occurs with vomiting, and this is a sign that the bladder is full of urine like a rain; and there appears gravel, and the patient groans with pain in the side, and he urinates many times, and then grows pale; and with these vomiting there is a foundation. And it is light to cure these vomiting until they are three years old; and it is very difficult in old people, and is as if one was mad between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	When we come to treatment, if it is necessary, first cleanse the patient with a lukewarm bath to draw out all the worms that are in the intestines. For they obstruct never to touch the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the arms, and loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never again go up high; then make him sit between your hands apparent, and his hands should be loosened from his buttocks, so that the bladder is completely relaxed downwards; then ask him to cough and touch downwards again.</start_of_turn>
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, if you hurry now to seize above the stone. And if it does not prick at the touch of your whole hand, if the patient is old, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; then press on its foundation, and ask for the stone, and when you feel it in your palm, if the bladder is against the loin; then press above your palm, and the stone will come out either by itself or you will see it spit out.</start_of_turn>
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the ribs above, and with his left hand to grasp the skin that is below the ribs in the part where the size is taken; then insert the spatula covering, since this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the ribs above, and with his left hand to grasp the skin that is below the ribs in the part where the size is taken; then insert the spatula covering, since this is the shape: and pass between what is between the ribs and the foundation, not through the middle but along the left side; and keep two hands above the bone, and two hands either adjoined or on the foundation, and the size through if it is wide by going around, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the bone, not too great;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and by chance press if the hand or the foundation should be forced forward, that it should leap forward in the work; and threads that there is part of the bone or there are angles, and margins: if it is grasped to stir; and if there is part that is swollen, similar to a gland, round, from which issue is slight.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	When there are angles or margins at the circumference, make the size larger; and if it does not slip, know that you must grasp the nails which are as sharp as a file at the head, in order to grasp the stone if it does not escape; or you can use a curved instrument at the head. If you do not skillfully engage it, it will be too wide. If it is not properly secured, it will be like straining glass.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	When there are more than one stone, grasp the largest one at the belly of the bladder first, then hold it tightly, and then pull it out. The smaller ones can be taken out afterwards if there are any. If the bladder is large, cover it with silk and make a larger wound. For indeed, these things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out too much due to the swelling that his wounds cannot be closed; but whatever you do, if you try to pull out the nails without breaking them, you will tear the flesh as long as you pull them out piece by piece.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	When you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon’s blood to the wound, and hold it in place. Then put on a wet bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up to his chest and do not loosen the dressing until the third joint above.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have loosened it, if there arises much blood from the wound of oil and water, then treat with oily dynafinicon and oily basilicon, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if pus comes out of the wound and corrosion, and blood clots in the bladder, and either the urine is retained, which is known in part as without straining with the urine: then do you give your dose in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will cause the bladder to become swollen and burst.</start_of_turn>
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then lift the wound of water and easily and cautiously, and support it in every way you know how, until it is healed; and make sure that all the times you treat it, that you bind the edges together with sutures, and assemble the medicines above the limb.</start_of_turn>
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the bladder, and it is fixed, and the urine cannot pass; if the doctor of this whom I speak of above says that you should urinate many times, we will hear of the size for this treatment.
