Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and make two angles fixed in one vessel:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and bind it around the root of the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then press the piece of iron gently into the root, until it reaches the stone; and turn the piece of iron in the stone back and forth, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if the urine comes then, press your hand on what remains of the stone that is in the bladder. If it breaks, and spurts out with the urine, and if there is blood, this is the sign of the disease;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you do not wish to do this by any means, take hold of the limb above the joint and support the limb below, then push the limb forward between the two tendons, and pull it out forcefully, remove the tendon, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; and cure as long as it is necessary.
de la piere des femmes	If you do not wish to do this by any means, take hold of the limb above the joint and support the limb below, then push the limb forward between the two tendons, and pull it out forcefully, remove the tendon, and congeal the blood that is in the wound; and cure as long as it is necessary.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If the limb is ever dislocated in a woman, and if this has never happened before, then it is a serious cure, and is defended by two things: the first is that the woman is a virgin; the second is that one cannot find a woman who is truly learned who knows how to manage such a thing, even though she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman who is well learned in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman's thumb is thicker than the man's thumb, for in this case she can make a deeper cut and there is greater fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, since this is necessary, if you take a mistress who is well learned, and prick the thumb on, and if you do not find one, do not take any woman who is stupid; and present her with a dance that is well known in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command of her with inquiry of the thumb.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And watch well if the woman is a virgin: then you must push her thumb or foundation and inquire about the thumb; and if she finds it, if you constrain her from below her thumb, you must recommend that she put her thumb or with the patient, and want and press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If indeed it is true, if it is moved from the groin to the knee, as far as it reaches the root of the thigh; then grasp the foot on the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone, where it is usually visible; and feel the thigh in that part. Do not move the thigh above the foot or below, and let the size be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then tighten the limb to the size, if you feel the thigh is too tight so that the bone can break; and that many times I have seen bones break in this way: small and large, thin and thick, rough and smooth, long and round, and which have a rough appearance. If the bones look similar, it is likely that there is displacement
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if it does not go away, if you put a broken glass vial inside and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, until the bone is broken, and have the instruments that I mentioned for extracting the arrow as a helper in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go by itself, and it is the artery that is severed, put the powder on the limb and bind tightly with thongs and bands, and do not attempt to move it again, but leave the wound alone until by chance the patient dies; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the bleeding has ceased and the limb is at rest, if you return to this work while the wound is still fresh, as long as the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	of hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as cheese, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and never is it properly in the belly of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case. And this is the membrane of the cheese between the white fat that we have said.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this membrane is from weakness that comes from the cheese, and it is spread throughout that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And never does it come from percussion on the cheese, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a pale yellow, or it is without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs of this assembly being complete, for if it is white and soft as we have said, if the abscess is round like the head of an egg, and does not bleed, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the very flesh, if the abscess is round with a portion of the yolk, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if the moisture is between the skin of the nails and the soft part, if one sees well; then when you see the colour of the moisture, if it fills all the surrounding parts, as it is before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, which comes after the introductor, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we bind them with iron, if it is judged that the patient is safe according to their poverty and the swelling of their body; then we anoint them on their back, on something somewhat high, and put a cloth under them;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	then we sit on their left side, and command the minister to sit on their right side, and extend the limb towards one of the two ribs towards the navel;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	For the fire that is on the body is hotter than the fire of the forge, and if it is too hot, it will make the wood burn and the fire will no longer be of benefit.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the face with a large hole, drain all the blood, and then put on your gloves; extend the face upwards; do not touch the beard, but only the face itself; carefully drain everything or in pieces immediately the cost of the vein, for if you do not drain it well, the blood will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood spurts out onto your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the operation of the vein; then join together the two limbs of the beard at a joint, and cure it as with the other wounds, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the blood corrupted by another illness, if you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then drain the wound thoroughly, and evacuate the blood, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if it is acute it is assembled in six parts together, rags which are six stems; if you have cut the other part just as you did the first one evenly, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound lint soaked in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	put another layer of lint soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the six nails, and put underneath doubled cloths, and tie up all around as it is fitting for this form:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use coarse wool according to this semblance and join them by stitching in the armpit, and one of the arms should grasp on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the shoulder; and the other two fingers on the two angles, and be all assembled with the restriction in the loop of the armpit.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is this cautery branch suitable for the size of iron, for you must take the cautery of the culter variety, and burn the hair of the testicles, and if it is eschaufed as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the poison is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and prick that membrane as with needles, and burn with this subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And if you burn in every way that you wish, until you have burned all; and keep that fire from touching the egg; and wash that this egg is more salve; and make sure to avoid discharge of blood, and that there is no swelling of the work.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if nothing hinders you, or incisions, or bleeding, or any other thing, if anything opposes your cure, do what is before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fainting, and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you threaten perforation, as I have said, and you are certain by the signs we have mentioned that the aquous humour is limpid,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	if you make the patient sit up on a chair that is raised; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with all the surrounding tissue wide open, and make the perforation deep enough so that all the pain is expelled;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put cotton on the limb and bind it, and leave until the remaining pain subsides; then cure the wound until it is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If white wool does not stop the pain at the root of the wound, if you should drink a penny or the instrument which treats the hydropic pain, as it is formed previously; and expand it, that is, pull out the wound, and soak that the pain returns, and assemble after about twenty days or when it has healed, and when it is assembled as before, and then the patient will recover his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the joints
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	The wounds that are in this section of the root are many in number, for it seems to me that their cause is that they remain there.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I will tell you of the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that abscesses often come from boils or corns, and sometimes from wounds; and this is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive heat and moisture, which is spread by boils or corns, or percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the urine; and finds no pain, and is an abscess of grief.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And by chance it is a greasy abscess with pus and blood, of a dark color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.</start_of_turn>
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the position of the abscess before the burn, when you press on it with your hand.</start_of_turn
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and do not touch it.</start_of_turn>
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	He who makes an incision in a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain on the two sides.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and can well make the size above this semblance, and above all others
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and that you bind like a cord the upper part, and the thread be of white silk, and deliver the hanging from all parts of the limb.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the limb is already swollen with these cords, if you must then treat the limb and bind it;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If it is loose at the socket, or within the vessels, then you must deliver all that is tense, and round off the edges.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the limb hangs loose from the socket or from behind, then you must grasp all that is taut, and pull out the root, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is finished, if you have used up the soft wool dressing in oil and rose wine, then cure it with other ointments until it is healed.</start_of_turn
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the bones.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient groans in pain as he walks.</start_of_turn>
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this disease is just as dangerous as this one before.</start_of_turn>
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and all that we say about it will be according to what the ancients have done.</start_of_turn>
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You must make the patient sit upright on the edge of the bed, then support the patient's head with your arms at their shoulders.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	At all the joints which are projecting towards the edge, grasp the master and extend them forward;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then hold the fractured limb wide open at the fracture, until it is uncovered,
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then draw out the bruised part, as we have said in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples;
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then I insert a needle or if there is double thread, I bind it to the first loop or the knot has come loose, and I bind it to the other end;
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	Then I grasp the cord in the middle directly, according to the length of the wound, and I draw out the corrupted moisture.</start_of_turn>
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	Then I treat the wound as usual or I cauterize it, if neither of these methods causes the bleeding to cease from either of the edges.</start_of_turn
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for in this way there is no harm done, and if all the blood vessels are coming, if you must, draw out the edges of the wound from all the blood vessels;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
de la routure dou syfac	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	If the vessel does not lose its nourishment by the incision of the veins, and if it dries and does not yield assistance.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	And the sign that it is a stretching from the socket, if there is swelling and swelling in the long term, and does not come immediately;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and is the swelling equal all the way up to the navel, because the socket presses on the intestine.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the socket is inflamed, that it makes an immediate sharp pain, and the swelling is diverse, sometimes the skin is pale, and this is because of the escape of the intestine and the stiffness of the socket.</start_of_turn
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never is the bone moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is pressed, and makes great pain for the patient, even when it is pressed.</start_of_turn
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire and fear, for it is known that they must be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And thus, if you command or patient must hold the intestines towards their belly in the wound, if they can be returned there;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then either suspend them on their collar between your hands, and hold the thighs together;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then extend the arm at the shoulder, and grasp all the skin of the armpits long;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	Then from the depth of the wound comes an amount suitable for the size of the wound according to what you must have learned by opening the wound, and so be it that the blood spurts out with such force.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	Then withdraw the sponge that is soaked in the leather of the intestines, until the white sponge of the gut is uncovered from all sides
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	Then insert your two fingers into the gut where the white sponge is soaked in the leather of the gut, between the white sponge and the second sponge that is soaked in the leather of the gut
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and pull out what is behind the egg, and between the second sponge; and grasp with your right hand from the belly of the intestines, and extend the white sponge upwards towards your left hand, and hold the egg against all the sponges towards the size of the wound.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	And command the minister to extend the arm upwards, and loosen what is above the limb.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	And look at his belly if there is any entrail or white fat adhering to the limb, and if you find nothing, if the bulge is in the belly, loosen it.</start_of_turn>
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	Then take a needle or if there is thick thread made of twenty threads, and pass it through the back part of the fat, which is behind the skin of the buttocks; then tighten, and cut off the ends that appear from the threads, until there are three threads left.</start_of_turn
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	Then assemble one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the fat, which we have said is behind the skin of the buttocks, with a strong thread of six parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then embrace the head of the shoulder, and bind it firmly in place with three parts, so that no vessel other than those that nourish it can enter the wound, except for incisions.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And straighten the limb according to the first limb which is long three times that of this one, and afterwards these three limbs leave the skin soft like the coat of a dog over the great bones of the thighs
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	And afterwards all the rest according to the curve which the heel bears; then bind the part which is over the skin of the thighs, as much as it is without pressure, and bow it, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	Then apply soft wool soaked in oil to the wound, and put on dressings, and I recommend applying pressure to the area we mentioned earlier.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the flesh except as we have said, after the incision, in doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this often happens, and leaves the limb until it bleeds through; and if it is delayed in healing, if it is raised from lukewarm water, and put on what we have mentioned, until it bleeds through;
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernias of the intestines.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter, I have never seen anyone cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the old people say that it is made like the hernia which is in the gut, in part like tying the veins, after the size above lightly to the belly;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cover it in me, and cure the abscess of what causes it, as long as the veins groan; and cure it as we have said, as long as it is sane.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Never comes routine in anger, as we have said, and open the lids; and do not see any intestines as companions, and if there are any, it is enough, and repair them at all hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and if it stays too long in this place, if one believes the wound or abscess, as long as the intestines are seen;
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	and this comes from the stretching of the flesh which is in anger, as we have said, because it is stretched, then is softened and relaxes the lids and opens
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and it is cured if by cautery, as we have said before; and never by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is that the patient lies prone on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the route that is swollen with a large hand according to the quantity of two fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then grasp the scapula which is below the skin that covers it, and take a hold and withdraw the limb that appears from the scapula.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the navel, then cut the two large veins that appear from the scapula on the top of the hand, and cut one and the other
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then withdraw the arm, and do not cover the scapula or extend the bone or anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the hernia of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then cure by the treatment of wounds. And when you close the wound, if the blood flows and cures the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is confined, and has no apparent cause in the course of treatment, and the cautery is useless in this situation, and more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the nails
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the nails is softened in baths of warm homes, because the nails that are within become softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it being cured, to make the patient lie on his back, and to remove the softened skin from the natural skin; then assemble the layers together with a suture, and if you see, sew up the excess of softened skin at two or three sutures firmly; then close between the sutures, and cure as with the other wounds, until it is healed, and take out the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The fire cautery. The cautery is performed by stretching out the best in hot water, until the hairs are softened and limp; then grasp the hairs at the root with your hand until they are returned and no longer feel.  For large cautery: grasp the limb firmly, pressing the skin of the joints with your left hand; then tie the suspension over the joint, and apply pressure with one finger at each crease, until they are well secured; and leave no mark on the surface of the vessels.  This method of cautery is milder than that by traction, for in traction there is always a risk of damaging the hairs, which the limb naturally desires to remove.  Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermofrodie est selonc deux manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les deux coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine. Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et deux coions. Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.
de la tentigene	Hermofrodie is according to two ways: one if between the two testicles opens as with the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in between they urinate. And the other way if in women, and has on the navel as a boy and two testicles. And the cure for the womb and fame if it is that you copulate the testicles all, and cure as other wounds; in the second way, men whose urine jumps through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a swelling above the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand, and this is the cure. It is fitting that you hold the excess of the tenting to your hand or wrist, and copulate it lightly; and do not be too rough, for discharge of blood does not come, then the cure of other cures while it is sound; and another thing that comes from the root of the marrow, and the navel, and sometimes jumps out, and is like the semblance of a bladder, and for this reason it is called the old "bladder disease". If it is fitting that you copulate it, as we have said the tenting, and cure it while it is sound.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	When the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
des emorroides	des emorroides.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroids are tears in veins which without support are not usually seen; and when old become tough. And we have said concerning the marks and signs, I will say here those which are useful for cure. I say that emorroids and tough veins, when they are pressed in the marrow, and they are not felt, if not except by the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the heel and press on its root, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw its pieces an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and assails, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is an opening at the back, and there are clots that look like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make an opening at the root. And when the wound is healed, if it is cured of swelling as long as it is healthy; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if it is covered as I have said the tough veins; and then it is cured as long as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	Emorroids are tears in veins which without support are not usually seen; and when old become tough. And we have said concerning the marks and signs, I will say here those which are useful for cure. I say that emorroids and tough veins, when they are pressed in the marrow, and they are not felt, if not except by the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the heel and press on its root, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw its pieces an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and assails, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is an opening at the back, and there are clots that look like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make an opening at the root. And when the wound is healed, if it is cured of swelling as long as it is healthy; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if it is covered as I have said the tough veins; and then it is cured as long as it is healthy.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Emorroids are tears in veins which without support are not usually seen; and when old become tough. And we have said concerning the marks and signs, I will say here those which are useful for cure. I say that emorroids and tough veins, when they are pressed in the marrow, and they are not felt, if not except by the cure by iron. Those which are at the mouth of the marrow, we can feel, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then extend the heel and press on its root, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw its pieces an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is blood, if she sits in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix with honey and assails, and make one application on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, if there is an opening at the back, and there are clots that look like wounds; then take lint, and soak it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make an opening at the root. And when the wound is healed, if it is cured of swelling as long as it is healthy; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is similar to a rough beard, if it is covered as I have said the tough veins; and then it is cured as long as it is healthy.
de l’enfantement	De l’enfantement.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	From infancy. A master first of all must know the figure of natural infancy, and its signs are when you see a woman pressing down on her belly and desiring to smell the scent: then the child is in haste to be born; so that his limbs are in the natural position, and his head comes out first, and supports him; and when you see these signs, if you press gently his belly, so that the child comes out headfirst; for when he descends on his head, if he is supported by his second hand, and the mother is comforted by his superfluities by a natural birth; and this is not otherwise. For it never comes from its knees or from the hips, or from the hands, or comes from his belly or from behind, and is converted by chance from his collar and by other harmful figures; if the master is at the dance that he is wise and subtle in these things, and warns of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures that we must aid in.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out headfirst by natural birth, and the woman gives birth fiercely, and his strength is weak, if you make her sit on a seat, or the women hold her; and arises her nature from oil or fennel, or whatever is in use, and then resume the dance between his two legs the little heel which is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	Fende the secondine, and clamp her nail as long as the moisture that is in her core is forceful; and press her belly until her fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle of fennel with oil of poppyseed; then make her vomit and expectorate of phlegm, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if the fetus is now gone. And if her two hands issue forcefully, if you must, keep them lightly together without tension; and if they will not enter, put the woman on her side, and hold her feet high; then withdraw the side to the earth, and hold her, that she does not bleed; and if her hands will not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you clamp her hands at the wrist that is in front, and pull out the fetus, and calm her equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	From the issue of the child from her feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the fetus comes from her feet, if you can push upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then the head of the shoulder turns back and forth, as long as it is even;
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	and then it grasps and extends back and forth.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it leap up to its armpits, if the order has grasped it, and makes it cough up the phlegm?
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if it leaps up further, God be praised.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	If it is not forced, as we have said, if the limb hangs too far forward or backward, as long as it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For in such a case it is readily done.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	If it is not forced, as we have said, if the limb hangs too far forward or backward, as long as it is in accordance with the natural figure. For in such a case it is readily done. And if there is force, as we have said, take muscle of elevation, oil of lint, gum masticated, and broth all together in a mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and put on the woman’s body and drive out this swelling.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then let the patient sit upright in a cold bath until the ribs are relaxed;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	When it is moist, let her drink one spoonful of myrrh, and let her drink, and leave her for an hour.
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	Then let her sit on a chair, and then make her spit and strain her mouth and throat, and gently touch her belly, for she is vomiting now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	because of the discharge from the child on his genitals.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this form, if he places his hands and feet together;
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then either he groans on his neck, and stretches out his tongue, and holds his breath.</start_of_turn>
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	and he folds his hands together and puts his hands on his belly, and grasps the nipples below, until they are apparent in the throat.</start_of_turn
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	and if the infant does not spit, take his hands and move them, then move his belly up, then take his hands away;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	And the woman must hold the child close and close; and command the woman to stay until the children are gone.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	And from the issue of the child who comes out with a large hand during
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I command you to engage to bring the hand back:
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	and if you cannot bring it back, if you must raise the woman, and call for help;
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If it does not return, if you manage it on the little lip, and you loosen the legs,
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	then restore the muscle that I mentioned earlier.
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	and if it still does not move, if you manage it on the little seat, then study the way to bring the limb back into place.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	and keep the limb still in its natural position, and make it evacuate naturally, and command it to stay as long as it feels pain.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child on his shoulder, and he has spread out his hands, and his face turned towards his mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	I believe that the baby is grasping your hand, then turning back and forth, and looking down lightly;
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when he is even, if you put on the muscular nature of elevation and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves back and forth;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, if you make it sit on its seat, and command it to grasp; and make it spit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	From this same measure at all the second degree.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes from this measure at all the second degree, if the second degree rests on your nail, as long as the moisture is emptied;
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the nail of the foot is bent over its face and its collar, if the nail of the heel is loosened, that it is not retained, and the patient dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then take out the child, as long as you have put it as it should be, and command the woman not to move at all:
adonques si istra legierement.	Therefore, if it is easily displaced.
de l’issue des gemelz	it must be reset immediately.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	it is not strange that this should happen often and always happens
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	indeed not.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that, when multiplied, they are torn apart by the syrup that begets them, which is bound to the bud.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and never comes out so naturally as one of them all, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it comes out grasping, if the treatment is as we have said, and whether it is the subtle dance, and makes toast and lightly touch what it does;
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	make her do as she is worth saving.</start_of_turn
de plusors enfans	Moreover.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Moreover, there are often formed in the marrow, that is to say, once, twice, thrice, or four times, or five, or six, or seven, or more just up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measure of the Savior’s grace.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is obvious that the Savior will save all these things, because by chance similar things happen;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	if you do as it is commanded
de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman in childbirth who has had a stillborn child or miscarriage, if as I have said in the division, and there is no urgent need, and you are constrained by the work of your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	you must consider that the woman is of sound mind and has no accident or is not in a state of imminent death; then you must order that she rest for a while and apply cold compresses to her face and chest.
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	if it is necessary that the woman should lie on her back, and her arms folded across her chest, and her legs raised up;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And the minister should grasp the hand of the boy, or if she is bound to the bed, until she is treated in descending order from the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then wipe the mouth of the patient with moist hempseed oil mixed with alum and fennel seeds and linseed seed, and then anoint her hands with these oils and these poultices.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then bind her lightly in the bath, then give her one or two baths with the unguents that are convenient for her,
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care that the child does not fall out of bed.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	If the nails are clenched in the eyes or in the nose or in the mouth or in the beard or pluck the hair or force it out with pliers or grasp the teeth,
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the eyeballs burst out on the face, the nails are driven or pierced and the teeth are loose;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary to keep the nail in the right hand, and put the thumb between the two of the left hand, and hold it gently, and insert the nail into none of these places that we have said, until the swelling has gone down
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	This is the form of the nail:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then the flesh finds another support, or the third time you have intervened, if the extraction is equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then it extends equally by moving from side to side, because of moisture, and the teeth of the bones are loosened by moisture, as is the form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if a part of it remains, if one must move a little of its fat, and put it in that part, and treat the other part;
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if there is no remaining part, if one must place this support or higher up again, and do so until it is all gone.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be retracted by stretching,
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	so you must wrap around with the drape until it is whole again.</start_of_turn>
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	then you must grasp in the joint of the limb or at the root, and thus you must do in the other hand, and hold the two feet.</start_of_turn
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	and if the child's shoulder is large and it is stretched out at the root, or if there is swelling or pain assembled,
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If it seems to you that you have dislocated the bony prominence between your two arms, grasp the head and strain the pain;
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you bind it with the instrument which is called “almidach,” from which it is formed with the instruments or bandage which follows this;
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	and thus make it swell naturally with great pain;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	and then treat for the bones as if they were tenailles,
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the head of the shoulder leaps out violently and is strained by force, if it is fractured, as much as the moisture that is or is about to issue out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it cannot be held back, if the bone is broken into pieces by the force of the muscle you must force it back into place;
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is swollen in the belly or if the ribs are fractured, if you must pierce as much as the moisture departs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is swollen above its feet, if the attraction is slight, and the movement towards the mouth of the marrow is less arduous.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or the hand, it is best to drain it away; that is to say, to uncover the covering that is wrapped around the limb.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	and keep the belly or the hand until the moisture that is in it has drained away.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if any other limb is fractured and the limb is displaced,
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	if the limb is pulled from the socket by the force of the marrow, and is treated until the marrow is exposed at the mouth of the socket.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	Then indeed, I shall anoint or apply oil, and I shall set to work.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the marrow is retracted by the hot cautery which has come, if I cannot bear to travel,
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	then I must bring moist and fatty things;
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and I shall bring sponges, and soak in soft water and moisten.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the shoulder is above its socket, and you must set it even, if you anticipate what we have said of the living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if it does not yield, if it breaks through in pieces, do not leave anything of the second [substance].
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And when you have done this, if you anticipate what we have said concerning the aftercare of patients who come into the hospital;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	and if discharge of blood occurs, if there is any restraining restraint, and if there are other cures.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb two infants were conceived, and as soon as one was born, the other expelled it.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came a swelling in her belly, and it burst open, and it began to swell greatly
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I called for help, and I thought for a long time, and I could not stop the bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong dressing, and blood came out, and after a while another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel at mouth, for this belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I want the wound, and by handling bones, as long as the woman is improving;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and saw the woman long tense in pain, and that was almost the end of her life;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have never known of this chapter except for the fact that when the master finds an unusual thing, he seeks help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Then comes the form of the pressor, as we have read in the books; and there are two returns with two thumbs of the two fingers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	However, the horns are either more subtle or more restrictive, and are made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	et soit li bouche dou fust, i.e. doi de large, et li marge des arbres, i.e. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi.
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and let the lips be wide, i.e. two thumbs wide, and the edges of the teeth must be firm, and long half a palm.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and these two adjustments are held in the mouth of the marrow to open when the two corners are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the resemblance of the teeth;
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	And he has as twice as many joints in the armpit, as you see, of a palm’s length, and two of a large size.

Then move your hand over all the instruments, if as you have done before you have held them equally, according to the quantity that you see the mouth of the arm open, until it makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very sharp, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one beholds them appear, the work hastens, and the height of one's home increases in proportion.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not fear the instrument except when it appears, for its need is not easily dispensable
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained at infancy, if you command the patient to retain its wing, and then make her expel it with conditions, and strain your hands to the mouth and the nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and if she jumps for this, well is it.

toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	All these herbs, or some of them, be boiled or put in hot water over the fire; then put a scab or hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the mare,

de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation

de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation

Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the persistent fistula at its foundation, and does not miss it.</start_of_turn
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you bite your thumb or foundation, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.

dou fremit	indeed.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice is a small appearance that is planted before the limb, and goes out like a worm.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice never bites, yet it is perceived as dead weight all over the limb, and comes to all parts in greater quantity than in other places.
