And if you see that it is done with a needle or iron in this fashion, and be discreet of your steps and cautious of your hands, do not pierce, for it must be held firm, and must be pressed. And if you see that you have cauterized too far forward or behind the cautery, stop immediately.</start_of_turn>
de la forme dou clistere	And if you see that it is done with a needle or iron in this fashion, and be discreet of your steps and cautious of your hands, do not pierce, for it must be held firm, and must be pressed. And if you see that you have cauterized too far forward or behind the cautery, stop immediately.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	And never make a blister of silver or gold, or of lead or tin; and never make of these instruments petty and great, according to these to which they are brought.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is due to a wide belly, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and if the belly is pierced or split, if you see, and the shoulder is fractured at one side and the hip at the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	or if you put medicines in a vessel of lead or parchment, or if you pierce all around the fracture,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And between each hole [in the cautery burn] there must be space, then stretch in these holes a strong thread of strong thread twisted ten or twelve times, and assemble the belly as if it were a nail.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the physician is inside, if he has a strong thread before a needle, then clip it; and that is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the physician neither too hot nor too cold, and join the head of the clip with oil or ointment of egg, or a similar thing, and then hold it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the physician grasps his hands together and holds them together until it is seen, then pull out the clip, and leave the patient his legs at rest,
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the physician sees that the pain is severe, if it is urgent; and if he sleeps all night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he sees it in the disease of falling of the belly, and the physician hastens to go out, if he recommences as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if it is bleeding from the veins or abscesses or incisions, if it is as subtle as with a child.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of a subtle bruise when the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in this section the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on the way they are made, and depending on the parts of the body from which they are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by biting of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or of lance or fist or knife, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	Or that they are made in accordance with the laws of nature, as in the case of wounds which occur on the neck, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, or other members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	And I will tell you of the cure for a wound of the head, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory of them will come to mind in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or a wound of the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that there is no breaking of stones or other things, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	And you doubt with certainty of incision: if you do it too much, the head of the sufferer will grow sicker from the wound itself; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the part that is wounded.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and listen to the patient’s swelling of wine and meat that is bad.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not see better, if either his meat is diminished, and he does not drink wine, does not eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and take out the wound, if it comes out, with wet cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	If there is no surrounding tissue around the wound, put a bandage on it if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, or anything else; I will tell you about that later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it has been moved, put on some ointment, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like the size of a nail and similar, and the layers do not want to stick together by tension, if you join them together with stitches, as I will say for wounds on the belly, from the stitches.</start_of_turn>
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered from bone and hangs by a thread, and holds only by a little, if you break it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hair instead of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And instruct the patient to eat nourishing foods, such as testicles and wheat germ, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find or smell decay, and it is not on the bone, if you cut around it all, and wipe away the pus, then it will heal
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without support cannot be held by medicines, if you find the artery and it is dislocated, if you tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if that does not help, if you burn it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if the cure is legitimate: put on this powder which binds just as well as if it had moved them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; white chalk three parts, and the powder thoroughly
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the wound, and hold it firmly, until it is well closed and reunited with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then bind it well, and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for we do not open medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we make this charcoal burn only, when we have no incense or blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if we do not put on this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but put on some edible substances or poulps of barley flour made of water and honey, until it bleeds profusely.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other cures until it is healed.

de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the head.</start_of_turn>
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes with the head and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the neck or the artery is cut.</start_of_turn
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, if there is no other remedy except to leave the wound open, do not put anything restrictive, for it will cause the nerve to retract; it is better to leave it open.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	Do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of its course is with the brain, which is the most vital part of the body

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of lance or knife</start_of_turn

les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common costings often arise in the costing of the belly,

por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be blunt;

k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they break and open the wound before the suture.

Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second costure is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and that you gather together the hairs of leather and the hairs of silk together with a thorn or there is a strong thread in the middle;

et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between the stitches the thickness of a small thumb
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture will hold the flesh,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sew a wound like this which has been opened or burst,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	Who was the master of the knife?

et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I held the wound closed for .xv. days, and the pain subsided, and he was healed.</start_of_turn>

Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of treating this ailment is that of Galiens the physician.

Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The wound is judged if it is like other wounds.</start_of_turn>

Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	If the limb is found whole; then put one finger in.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	If the limb is found whole; then put one finger in,
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	If the corruption is in the joint, if you touch the corrupted joint and support the bone from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	If the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other limb except that which covers;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is from the hand or from the foot, if it is very strong in this matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but in any case you must inquire about the origin of that corruption, how it appeared to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and keep still in every way possible, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and that the cuts and sutures that cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of pain,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their greatness and their subtlety, and their size and their fineness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And because of this, it is prudent to appear with some resemblance of work when one possesses the instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and the objects that the work will show you are the instruments you will need, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you think of the instrument which you must employ in this case, according to what it is able to do.
dou feu	If you think of the instrument which you must employ in this case, according to what it is able to do.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, or by excessive force, or by violence;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	when you have treated the dislocation by medical means, and it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if it is certain that covering that limb up to the root or the decay comes,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient escapes by that of death, or by malice, which is greater, from the defect of the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	then follows the blackness, and then comes the decay of the limb.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And grasp it throughout the body; if you are hasty in covering,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if there is percussion of venomous creatures, such as scorpions of the sea, vipers, and the like.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the bite is on the head, do not give it any space to come until the hand arrives.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	and if it comes up to the hand, if the bite has reached the joint, so that the dislocation does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, if the thumb catches on the cuticle; and if the thumb passes the cuticle, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And it is of no avail to threaten fiercely except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and whatever is done when corrosion comes or when the thumb comes: if the thumb comes before the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or if the thumb comes, if the thumb holds all the thumb;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it [hair] mounts in the leg, if it reaches the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes from below the knee, if there is no other pain but that of leaving the patient dead;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and you must bind the limb above and below and keep it still and quiet
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one finger of the lower limb and another finger of the upper limb,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you must uncover the flesh which is between the two joints, with a broad spatula as wide as the bone is uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then pull out the bone or marrow, and put a cushion of lint around it so that the bone does not touch the sound flesh,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring the patient other pain and incisions.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	and if blood comes out when you are working, if you cauterize the tissue sufficiently,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put upon some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb firmly with a secure bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you of a home remedy for this:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	there was a blackness that seemed to burn like fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And that corrosion first occurs in the marrow of the bone, as it consumes the entire bone.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the bone is affected by the corrosion, if it covers the bone and is sound;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	it returns to me, either the corrosion or the hand, and it comes to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on it things that impede the corrosion, and I cannot stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	He says that I should grasp his hand, and I will not, for I fear that I will only worsen the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	I also doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the strength of the man was weak; and he awoke all, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he covered his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have not heard of such a thing concerning fire except for that which we do for other purposes when necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does it happen that I open a vein without causing swelling, and it remains so long that it makes great gathering of blood.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and bursts open, and in that leap blood escapes, and stays confined within the vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin which is below is just as subtle as a veil of fine linen.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And do not move beyond the bone, beyond the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And are not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it becomes so prolonged that it reaches the bone and breaks through, it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and if you grasp that skin tightly and even when it is subtle, like a veil;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And it does not matter to me for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have sworn that the skin is corrupted, and the corruption is not in vain,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	if the skin is thick and tough, as in a burn, when the scab has formed:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the wound is large and if the odor is unpleasant,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Then take oil, assails, and beeswax equally, and mix them together in one vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	While the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take according to your need, and make it into a liquid with honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And in loosening the shoulder, and straining the part;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine rest for an hour and a half, then take it out while pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this three times, until the shoulder is relaxed and the bone is loosened.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and never with lukewarm water.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	When this medicine is not present, and you take a handful of wine must, and drink water from above,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let the fluid flow, and clench your fists, until you believe the pain has gone away.</start_of_turn>
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear the pain, neither Egyptian medicine nor the must of wine will help.</start_of_turn

et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure.</start_of_turn
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then let go of those things that corruption has embraced, and makes an imprint in the bone, or has stiff limbs, or has caused damage;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If the surgeon who performs the fistula cure, as we have said before.

Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	A fistula is a hole that arises from the abscess due to a pouch of the hand

Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Two thumbs which arise from the hands of certain men by chance are always fleshy.

Des vils	A nasty lot.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large vessels enclosed in fatty matter filled with black bile, which comes together in greater numbers on many limbs affected with pain.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often in the legs of those who walk and work and bear burdens, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you do not give any purgatives of colchicum, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	Iron is cured in two ways: one is with vinegar, and the other with black bile.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And thus too, if you ligate the vein and force it through, do so with all your might.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	And thus too, if you ligate the vein and force it through, do so with all your might.The size of the wound is as follows: first, grasp the limb firmly with a warm wet hand, so that the greater part is not stripped bare,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	and then strain the limb of the patient from below the hip joint up to the part below the knee.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	and then clamp the vein in one, two, or three places, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then believe and grasp firmly the black blood from your hand, from the tip to the base, as many as there are without causing pain to the patient who can suffer enough already.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	Then hold it [the blood] and command that it clings to the black fat;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Then repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do no harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The food of this kind: open the limb of the patient, if there is hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then he puts in the bath or washes him, and he raises the limb of the acute heat so that it becomes red, and swells the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If you do not have a bath, if he is burnt by the fire, then hold his hand over the vein at the long end of the elbow, or in the lower part at the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then he covers the skin with ointment, and tightens the vein from the chest downwards, until it appears when you feel it
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	Then you see it red and black, and when it comes out or the skin seems like a white thread;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then stretch the limb again, until it is freed from the skin, and then pin it with a light bandage.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then stretch the limb once more in another direction two fingers; then pinch the skin over the wound until it opens wide.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then hold the limb still, as you have done before, and pin it with another bandage, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then stretch the limb once more, or several times if necessary, and then hold it still, and pinch the skin around the wound, and then hold the limb in place, and hold the wound still.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then the tract and hold the juice until the second size; then remove the size by size, until it is all gone, then finish off.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you do not manage to pull it out and lift it, if there is a thorn with all its barbs left,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and pull it, and there will be some blood, and turn your hand from side to side until it is gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and keep that it does not swell, for if it swells, if it cannot be pulled out or lifted, it comes to harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have treated it thoroughly, if you take out the wound dressing of coarse wool in wine and oil of roses; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the limb is contracted and twisted and covered together, and is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Then you must stretch it out violently, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The limb's form which we cover with a bandage is crooked, and must not be broken, only the bone must be covered;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	And it is of great concern, for if it were slight, it would close the vein; but whether large or small, as we have said, this is its form.
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enclosed in the limb, in hot parts or where there is no herb or tree, and in the earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and sometimes it happens elsewhere except in the limb, and this comes from the decay that comes from the rotting of the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	If it comes from the belly towards the neck, seize between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if there is a sign of great swelling of this vein, if it comes into the limb, there will be a very great inflammation.</start_of_turn>
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then it contracts the limb, and the vein bursts like the root of a plant.</start_of_turn
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the limb is opened, if you advise that you wrap around it with a piece of cloth about the size of three and a half, from the armpit to the groin, and the knot,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and leave the hair on the limb, and every time that it has reached its limit of growth, if the surrounding tissue engulfs the hair and the root, do not cover the root until it is fully expelled.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, if it returns to the flesh, it brings about inflammation and pain or pus, and makes the disease worse
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it must be treated promptly and without delay, and nothing of it should remain or be left behind.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And it is never this vein that is treated with five palms of length, or with ten,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And it is never this vein that is treated with five palms of length, or with ten; and one must know that it comes out for ten palms of length, and when you grasp it, if there be even a hair’s breadth or a wound, and the blood spurts to the end.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if all this is done; and that the matter within is evacuated, and medicines are brought to the place, without causing any further pain, then the wound is cured like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And never with this vein are hands rained, and even when it bursts through the joint of the elbow, or in the armpit,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And thus comes forth from the wound, and from that it leaps; cure the same as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And thus comes forth from the wound, and from that it leaps; cure the same as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	And thus comes forth from the wound, and from that it leaps; cure the same as we have said before.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And thus comes forth from the wound, and from that it leaps; cure the same as we have said before.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And he senses all too well the approach of a limb, when it breaks the skin or it goes through, and leaps forward.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And is infected with the putrefaction of humors, as when they come near and serpents and worms and flies or the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubts its malice, for when it goes through the flesh, and it reaches the head, and comes to the marrow,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	it returns by chance, and destroys the marrow; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if one cannot force it until it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	when you must indeed tie up the limb above and below with a strong and firm bandage.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then you must force upwards and outwards, and if it does not budge, do not delay,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you must burn with fire until it is dead.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harms it makes when it corrects the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming or close to the oil, if it tightens the eyelids, then shut your eyes tightly and pull away from it.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and you must order the patient to take nourishment of nourishing herbs for the bad humors that are carried
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and abstain from eating meats that are corrupted.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes of wind-sitting
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the joints of the limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and therefore moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and discovered her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And thus afterwards, the limb will rise up like a worm at the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more tense than anything, like living silver when it breaks from its bone to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that limb and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then afterwards corrected throughout the limb, so that it comes into the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me that it twisted back inwards towards the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how it twisted back inwards towards the body, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I would rather that pain did not remain in one place than that it should move from one limb to another.</start_of_turn>
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I do not like it when I see it in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought that this was the reason why the woman had dry clothes and exposed veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this appeared that violent wind was restrained.</start_of_turn>
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not appear to me on this account with these people who are well-favored, who have dry clothes and covered veins.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see that this disease is cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the limb hangs limp and swollen, and then suddenly swells up as much as this wind-gust hinders the limb's ability to flex,
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure for this that bursts the wind-gust, such as foul pills and seraphim pills, and similar things.
Des saiettes	From pads.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The towels are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they relieve.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	There are various types of towels, some with large points, others with small ones, and some with hooks and loops;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with angles, and some with long handles, and some with fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	or in the main or the forearm it tears; ou qui sont trop pesants pour lor taille, ou trop fines pour lor puissance.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	If brain, head, liver, spleen, arm, leg, intestine, bladder, and other members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it happens in none of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must know that you must be wary of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these things are not recognized, neither the arrow nor the wound is properly treated, if only by chance it is cured.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of a fractured skull when the arrow pierces the bone, and leaps the substance that is above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when scraping, swelling, twisting, and bruising in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of wits, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and in some cases without cause, or from the ear; and by chance loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from a white wound resembling a boil, and as if burnt with fire;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this symptom appears to you, if you adhere to treatment, draw out the arrow if it is not entangled.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it is pierced or embedded is that it is close to the left breast, and that it feels as though it is fixed in something hard, do not see it empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow moves as well as the pulse, and in dark blood without, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	it is certain that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of a wound that never heals is that there is no scab on the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and sweats profusely.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow remains in the flesh, if it is taken out with difficulty, it causes great swelling and great pain and breathing; and the limb becomes limp
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrow comes out or remains in the flesh, by chance there is no sign of indigestible meat in the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	If the arrow comes out or remains in the flesh, and there is no sign of feces in the intestine, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the stone in the bladder is dislodged, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, and the patient experiences great pain: the wounds are mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpit, the groin, the buttock, the thigh, and the leg are affected, and the like, there are many possible causes.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the stone is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I have mentioned before.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There is one house in which a stone or drool hangs from the root of a nerve:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and its trail on the other side of the ear, and it was cured without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And there was a play of an arrow that fell into the marrow on the side of the ear,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was retrieved, and did not reach anything but the tip towards the head,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and was of a Turkish bow, quite large in size; the play was successful, and there were no bad consequences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take out an arrow from the throat to a crest, and the Arab arrow was in the ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I grasped the barbs, and pulled it out as stealthily as possible, and the crest was saved.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from my side, which was in the hip or belly, and I thought it was going to die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after a few days, I found that it had not passed;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the splinter, and the marrow, and the bone marrow, and not in vain.

ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	it finds no rest in any of its natural works.

et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and thereupon he suffered great pain; and there were many other symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	and thus it was with another man, who had an arrow in his face, that the king’s prince was struck in the eye by it,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was completely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I hasten to the treatment after it is complete two days hence. If I find the wound much too large, I shall delay the treatment.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I shall attempt to do it all cautiously, and I shall not feel it myself;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there is no longer any pain or tingling in the ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of the arrow that was causing this
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place upon the limb a plaster that is both adhesive and digestive, so that the limb does not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I see the limb go limp from the wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the dressing again, and closed the wound, and comforted the patient for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the wound still throbbing in his side; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply the corrosive medicinal salve to the wound by hand every day until it subsides.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I hold the eye shut, and feel the tip of the arrow which must be withdrawn from the body;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I support the wound by means of that corrosive medicine until the tip of the arrow becomes visible again;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and let it remain covered for three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then he expands if the wound that I touch with my thumb and my little finger, and I cannot hold it still.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	therefore I must continually twist and contort in various ways, until I grasp it firmly with my thumb and little finger
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I hold it, and I will restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it immediately, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Or you have said the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your remedy on that which I do not understand, for these books do not teach me everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but you know masters better than anyone everything that is great and that which is present and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Trueve neuf ouvertures, et neuf instruments, au descendant des choses extraignes qui arrivent en ce travail.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	Nine new openings and nine new instruments; for the descent of the foreign bodies which arise in this work.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	...or by liquid or by some other means.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	...and that which remains by weight can never be taken out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, if you leave it as long as the hair is carried around the head, and be glad that it comes out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	Or if it is stuck in the bone and cannot be pulled out, if you leave it alone for some days, and move it every day.</start_of_turn>
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will come out, and if it does not come out, if you pierce around all around the circumference, as long as the limb is swollen, and then pull it out.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the sliver is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the belly of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And none of the accidents which I have mentioned above should the patient be urged to treat immediately; but he should leave them as they are until they have become even after some days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the scab comes up to the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	and if the scab only sticks to the bone and does not come up to the surface,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains with the patient some days without causing further harm, if the inflammation subsides.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the moisture-soaked flesh is fixed and will not yield, if you administer tarres around it as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	If the fleshy part is restored to its place with difficulty, if we cannot see it clearly, if it tries to force its way;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if the limb is not adequately braced
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you do not do so with the greatest care and attention to the wound and the dislocation.
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the wound is as great as the pain.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	if you pull out the arrow and there is an earlobe in the wound, hold it so that it stays put.</start_of_turn>
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if the bone that is pierced by the arrow is split in two parts at the root that you pull out,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	break or crush the ears of the arrow, as long as you can pull it out.</start_of_turn
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And subtilize well that you do not break the splinter, but rather grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not succeed at once, if the limb remains bent over, then grasp it firmly, for the extraction will bring relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding hinders you, contrary to what we have said in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	keep your hands away from the incision and the vein, and take care that you do not pull out the splinter dangerously.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Or castrate or tear, or firmly or mildly; and set the patient according to the form in which he was when the arrow flew in,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest aid that there is, and if you do not know what to do, if he is showing you what to do, do it as he signs.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or he opens nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in the place if one sees it or feels it suddenly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Thus do so, until the nails can take hold, and then extract it: if the pain comes now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be loosened, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it is forced out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is a splinter of bone, if it has all been fractured;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if there is a break, and you see that it must be managed, if it is managed with a cutting instrument,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the point of the arrow enters the groove of the instrument; then hold fast,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is hooked, hold the instrument steady. That is, let the point of the instrument enter the wound, in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	and if the arrow is entangled, if you must, grasp the surrounding tissue or the poison is there, as you do.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as you deem appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	If the splinter is in the shoulder or arm, or in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, cover over it immediately, if you cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	Cover the wound and the nerve, then draw out the splinter, and then suture the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn>
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which we treat the splinters is similar to the beak of an eel, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the end of the bone is like the wing of a bird.</start_of_turn>
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push at the end of the arrow, if it is like this shape:</start_of_turn
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the nails to push and to grasp if it is like this:</start_of_turn
des voinnes dou cors communes	From common veins.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From common veins.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	From common veins. Namely: the jugular veins which are behind the ears and are covered by hair.
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the jugular arteries which are in the temples appear.
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And thus veins which are in the armpits of the eyes, which are called "aspire,"
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the back of the ear.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two armpits which are under the arm
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the veins which are on the sides of the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "augeherich."
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And thus veins that are sore to the touch of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that we commonly touch are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the chest, and is called the great vein;
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the third is called the “fast,” which is made up of the cephalic and axillary veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it the vein of the head, and if it is or is not straight along the coast,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call it the vein of the head, and if it is or is not straight along the coast,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that one from which one often sees, that opens manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	and the saving vein is the one that is between the auricle and the ring finger, and if it rains;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the limb or the heel are two veins: one if it is outside the prominence of the pocket of the left cost,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And in the limb or the heel are two veins: one if it is outside the prominence of the pocket of the left cost, and the second which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other limb are two veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to cause old abscesses to burst, and to expel foreign matter.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of the patient, as I have told you, is that you rejoice at the head of the sufferer,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rejoice at the head of the sufferer, or the veins are rough and tough; then stretch the patient's neck with a firm grip.</start_of_turn>
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	as long as the veins open behind the ears depend from the head.</start_of_turn>
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and if you feel pain in your side, or swelling, it is a sign of infection.</start_of_turn
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lancet, and insert it through the skin to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and insert it through the skin to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein, and hold the skin and the vein firmly. It must pierce through and cause blood to flow until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then take the lancet, and insert it through the skin to the bone, then keep your hand over the upper part of the vein, and hold the skin and the vein firmly. It must pierce through and cause blood to flow until you see; then strain and ligate, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And as I have already said, concerning the incision and the cautery, or the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The blood of the.ij. arteries that are in.ij. temples, if it is worth the ancient emigration,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The blood of the.ij. arteries that are in.ij. temples, if it is worth the ancient emigration,
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of health if it is like I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient is groaning with pain, as long as the.ij. veins open widely;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse throbbing in his thumb, and then he should seize it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then he should take hold of the limb above the thumb at the index finger, and hold the lancet near the base of the thumb,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and hold the vein high up, and close it, as you would for other veins, and do the evacuation of blood as needed;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then the thread comes, and you leave it as long as it remains whole; and as for that which we have spoken and its management and its extraction, or its beginning.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the cephalic vein in old diseases of the face, and in migraine, and in redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and if the patient strains his neck by twisting, as the vein is open.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called the “forceps,” which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point [of the cautery] on the vein, and hold it firm with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow out as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient’s collar and tie the vein until it is firm and never leave it open with a wide flame.</start_of_turn>
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not permitted for me to say that the flame should be too thick; and the same with the vessel, for the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.</start_of_turn
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the two veins that are in two palms if it helps with the swelling, and with the pain, and with the redness, and with the swelling in the oil, and has diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And if the patient has strained his neck by twisting from side to side, like before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the same, and if the blood is dark like the passage of a long flame over a wide area, for there is no fat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make pressure of blood as much as you can manage, and then bind above and below, and bind well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The blood of the vein does not taste like water, and has strong nausea, and has fevers,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If there is swelling and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	If there is swelling and redness that comes in the face, and even when it is old, and if the patient has strained his neck, then strain his jaw with your left hand.</start_of_turn>
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the fire from the long end, and insert it between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open easily, and without it will start to mend now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too far from the wound, but rather draw out blood as needed; then bind it for the night, for it is moist and restored by morning.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The blood of the three fingers helps to loosen the swelling, and to mix medicines, and to cure diseases, and to stop vomiting, and to corrode, and to cause herpes, and to cause tumors.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the blood is that when the patient pulls out his head from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And either the master stands above the head of the patient, and the patient sits upon his seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then he takes hold of the vein for a long time, and then he gives blood temperately, or as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then he makes the other part in the other vein, and then he ties the limb, and tightens all the middle veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not strangle; and he leaves it until morning, when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the blood of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and wounds of the arms, and toothache and pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before you, and strain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the palm of the hand, and look at the two veins, one of which is at the outside of the thumb and the other at the inside,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And we know them by this, that they are black, and that around them are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore, take them both together, and if you do not know them and are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if the larger one is at the shoulder and all the same make the three veins below and above, for this is the same way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the veins of the armpit the tongue is supplied.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins that are swollen with the tongue is of aid after the blood of the cephalic, and this is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and if the quality of the sick person is that the patient sweats between his hands before the sun, and he stretches the tongue, and looks towards the cost of the ribs, a black vein will appear:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then both of them will be black, and do not go too deep, for these are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins which we usually handle are commonly healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when pricked with a blunt flame, or olive-oil-soaked thorn, as with deep cuts, and is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and subtle according to the size and distance of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of the fire cautery is known to be round, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And must be skilled in opening large veins filled with visible blood, which contain much blood and trouble.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for healthier veins, or there is citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to relieve ailments such as thirst in the throat, and swelling in the throat, and pain in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is proper for the healer to remain calm, and to seize the artery which is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he seizes the artery, and blood spurts out, if he persists in holding, as I have said before.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not be afraid of the flame, but should hold firmly as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	and if the hair does not come away easily, as you should do if you must, and bind another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or do you wish no rain from it, or do you keep hold of it in your arm: it will open manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the handle of the flame is numb, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see that the blood vessel is known, if you must then stretch out your arm, touch the flesh as long as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the limb is closed, and then bind up your arm, and hold the vein with the flame numb.</start_of_turn>
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And take heed that you do not pierce the vein when you see the limb inflamed, for it is the vein: halt therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor transparent, know that it is without a vein: halt therefore.
