haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hastenedly hold your hand over its length, and keep your hand steady, then reset your limb if it is not stained; for many times it has happened to me.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	leave the limb still, and do not move it; and if you have any doubt, do not move it at all.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not stained, and it swells, and the medicine is not present, if the artery bursts, because the head of the humerus is retracted; hold it still without.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a bandage of silk, and bind it firmly, and take hold of one half and hold it firmly until the other half is reached
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	And if it is not stained, that is good; but if not, if the physician commands, as we have said, powders which stain blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stainings are not made greater by the greater quantity of the wound, and the power of the hand.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The blood of the vein flows much more readily if it is treated with the chief of the head above and the sides of the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said already.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary that the vein should be raised by the nerve which is below, and if it is not sufficiently deep, and the nerve is torn,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	it swells and the patient is either paralyzed or disabled forever;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some homes due to its subtlety, it is certain that you must use an instrument which numbs; and avoid that the nerve is injured at your poor.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if the vein is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The blood of the cephalic vein helps, that it attracts blood from the head, and helps with the swelling;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is certain to be safer to prick with the olive or myrtle flame, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Whatever, it is better to ask for help at the beginning, and do not grieve if it fails the first time, and we try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance it will happen to burst into tears in front of some people, which can happen the first time, but do not grieve it.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about health is that blood must only be drawn to preserve health.</start_of_turn
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And so to ward off future ailments.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the blood be drawn from one of the two veins which are or should be: namely, the cephalic, facial, or basilar.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And if it should be necessary to bleed in the beginning of a patient’s groaning, and in vomiting and sweating afterwards when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And if necessary, bleed the first or second hour, after an hour or two hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The blood which is administered for diseases has no fixed dose, but when necessity demands it, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and must not be given to infants less than 123 days old, nor to women who are pregnant for more than four months up to seven times.</start_of_turn>
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Must not be given to those who have passed 60 years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	and whenever anyone sees that they are suffering, in whatever way, it is prudent to keep their intestines free from any slight congestion.</start_of_turn
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If there is a tooth of madness retained, so that the veins do not draw intestines the superfluous humours carried by the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	if there is too much fat in the body, or if it is putrified, or if there is too much bile, or if there is an excess of urine,
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one should eat of something unhealthy after passion of the bowels, vomiting, and discomfort of the belly, and multiple emissions of urine, and pain in the belly, and toiling, and guarding, and grieving, and this all or by some weapon or poison;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtilize the humours, if they are not great, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have any power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter the bath, if nothing else hinders you, to subtilize the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and take from the vein some blood down to the wrist, as we have said before
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that work going, and prick, and linger, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and tie and bind them, and let the blood rise higher than the hand that we are holding, and wipe the arm once or twice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then is strange the limb above the middle, for when it is too tight or loose, it cannot be corrected without;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then the hand grasps the limb, so that the veins swell up, and one feels them there.</start_of_turn>
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the skin with a little oil, and put the thumb of the left hand on that vein below the limb, a little higher or lower as you wish.</start_of_turn
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not tear.</start_of_turn
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee as readily as cords to the physician, and if some are such as are filled with windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when one puts on the flame, when one takes away the flame, and cannot open the vein, then one is in this state.</start_of_turn>
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it bursts the vein, if the wound is too severe, for this it is advisable that the physician be warned in these matters.</start_of_turn>
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; if not, it must be repeated again either immediately or later, for if the patient is not relieved.</start_of_turn
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient begs, let him wait a while, either an hour or two, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	And indeed, if it comes to this, there will be swelling; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding when it stops.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	or if the limb is slightly dislocated, or if you suspect that it will not bleed as much as you see, if you are confident in the limb itself with all its fire directly over it;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	or the work is done carelessly, even if the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not immediately apply pressure to the bleeding, put on a bandage of oil, for it softens the body of blood, and makes it viscous in this limb where the oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus apply the oil bandage to the bleeding so that you stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and thus makes a trial and bow of blood, when you put it on the limb; if you take it off too soon when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	and if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are in a hurry, place the damp sponge over the wound and cover it with a cloth, and hold for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And make sure that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days, no blackening or greening, if it does not cause me harm.</start_of_turn>
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, do not put anything of aloe or mastic root in vinegar, mustard, or similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is abscess and appearance at the root of the nail: put your hand there, and if you feel the root soft under the pressure of your hand, if it is that kind of appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave off any article that is not essential to the meaning of the sentence.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And take out each piece of blood according to the amount of its virtue, and its color.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is dark without, if you leave it until it is red; and if you see it big, if you leave it until it is slight; and if it is too thick, if you let it cool down.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is proper for the one who is calm and strong, and has need of extracting blood, to make the wound larger, and let the flame be large.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, keep him healthy rather than harming him, and do so by cutting through, not by pricking.</start_of_turn>
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is useful for the decortification of blood and the compression of nerves, and is worth more than if the blood were long rather than wide.</start_of_turn>
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one who has cold feet, it is proper to give him soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is exhausted, give him two or three times the blood.</start_of_turn
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, let him eat before the blood soft bread soaked in sweet oil, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he prick at the blood, after the issue of blood clots, let him drink plenty of broth of herbs, and fragrant oil.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of blood clots.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees that his arm has turned pale, and he feels well again another time, if it is possible by great bleeding, let it rest still and still, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has strong swelling, if he remains thus for thirteen hours after the first bleeding, or after the twelfth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself well on one side, if he must remain well for the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the body which has already escaped, and it causes fever; if you can bear a great quantity, and expand the wound until it reaches the bone;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	For one must never do harm to the sick, but must teach them to live with the evil that exists;
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often happens when the patient is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not neglect that whenever you see the limb slip once, do not permit it to slip a second time, for the wound is closed, and pressing further will only increase the damage done;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the limb widely, for this is harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it as long as it remains loose; or you must point the tip of the cautery at the root of the vein, until the blood clot which is causing the pain has been broken through.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And put upon one hand a little thread that has been put in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it alone and do not restrain me, until the swelling subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood the second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is saved in place of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And if the patient’s hand is grasped in hot water, until the bruise is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it firmly, so that the vein opens easily, and leave it bound for a while, neither too wide nor too tight.</start_of_turn>
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if it cannot be cured, keep the hand in hot water again, and leave the bruise exposed in the water until enough blood has clotted.</start_of_turn>
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	or if you put the hand in too much hot water, it will swell more in this state than in the previous one.</start_of_turn>
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the blood of this vein is more precious than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The blood of the armpit of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand and immerse it in hot water, until the vein is emptied if seen;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you do it thoroughly and with all your might, if nothing is broken;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not be afraid too much of pain, for the nerves are all so exposed without flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And then put the hand back in warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will help to hold it together, and put on a bandage.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth to the disease of the mice, and do the same as I have said concerning the right side.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The blood of the armpit is worth for all the diseases that are outside the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	if like diseases of the marrow, and retention of blood, and disease of the veins, and swellings and old wounds, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this blood is that if the patient is suffering from acute pain, and rubs over the belly until it boils,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the belly is soft under the joint; and if the vein is at the ankle, and by lifting the limb there comes out drops of blood.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Healthy is the loin or more large vein, or at the ankle, which is swollen.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you touch it with your hand, if you feel numbness there, and if it is as if you were burning; be cautious.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it does not recover, if you reset the limb in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If you must do it a second time, for it is salt;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of force, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that is clotted.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its blood is that if the patient lies or bathes, and strains below the ankle three times,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, do everything in every way that you can, and cross it.</start_of_turn
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is better to keep the hair long, for it is stiff; and if you prick it at its root, keep your eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	Otherwise, if you do not keep it [hair] firm, if there is no sign of life in it that it should open or swell, and if it is toward the little toe, and you guard against nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	do as much to stop the bleeding as you see, and then loosen the knot, and put on cotton and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Vacuum therapy
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selon ces deux manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sang, ou sens ferir.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Venuses are made of horn, or spiderwort, or elderberry; and their ligation should be done in two ways: by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting only. And this ligation which is done by cutting if it is done in two ways: or it is very strong, or it is done with fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	or it is done with bleeding.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	or it is done with a cut at the root of the hair, or at the edge of the scalp; and the other is done with a cut at the root of the hair, or at the edge of the eyebrow.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And thus with others in both shoulders; and the suction cup grasps the beard of the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup grasps the armpits; and the suction cup on the nipples
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the suction cup grasps both arms; and the suction cup on both legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the suction cup grasps the ankles; and the veins do not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And for this reason, let no one fear me, for when we draw blood from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And for this reason, let no one fear me, for when we draw blood from a vein, it must be done without fire or pain, in no disease that comes from excess, until all the blood is evacuated.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if by necessity of disease it is necessary to draw blood, or by custom, if the physician administers it at the beginning of the month or at the end, and every month and every ten days.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they must draw blood, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if there be such as find swelling and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the collar, and dark circles under their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such as find a discharge of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit blood.</start_of_turn>
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there be such as dream, and see blood and vomit and water and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is wet and moist, we command them to fast for two hours after dinner.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The blood from the wound helps to alleviate the pain of the shoulder … that comes from these veins, and it cannot be done except after the evacuation of all the pus;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	… that if it is in place of the blood of the cephalic vein,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it cannot be done except in those who have a cold complexion or who have choleric temperament, for this makes them suffer greatly;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it must not be done in those who have or suffer from cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And if the patient is conscious, if he becomes dizzy, it is necessary to place the suction tube one place further down the throat due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The suctioning of the throat replaces the bleeding from the head and the vomiting, and for this reason it is useful at the end of the meal
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and at the swelling of the channel of the tonsils, and in swallowing, and at repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and the coving is necessary, because if it holds too tightly, it can cause dizziness or stomachache or pain.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The winds blow cold from the coast and cause pain in the chest, and pain in the head, and swelling, and constriction, and pain at the root of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	It is better to let the blood of the veins flow; and it is commanded that the patient place his hand on the artery, that he does not compress it, and does not cause any bleeding.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds blow cold from the coast and cause disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the health of the two upper teeth.</start_of_turn>
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds blow cold from the coast and cause disease that comes from heat and swelling.</start_of_turn
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The vents of the spleen are worth as much as two veins of the arms.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the patient not to fear that it will cause him too much pain, because it is made of flesh, and knows bones and arteries well.</start_of_turn>
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is worth as much as sores of the foundation, and has diseases of these, and it is advised that the wound be large and of hair, that it has much to do; and by chance, if it should be superficial, it would break; and this would make great wounds.</start_of_turn
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The veins of the legs swell widely open, for they draw blood from all parts of the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the kidneys, and of the bladder, and restore the flowers; and are in the place of the groin, and of the knee, and all of them expand the body afterwards, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the letup is that you apply it at once without delay, and do so steadily, and hold it firmly in place, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the limb turn red and swell, and expel the redness of blood; then withdraw, and reapply the letup, and take care of the position of the body, for there are many who have a tender scrotum, and clear pores: if you do but cut once only, and you make large wounds, and a large depth; and do so gently.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not thick, if you can cut twice: the first time to underlay the large blood vessel.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very painful, if you must inflict the wound for the third time; and when our wings are weary of carrying blood and blood, if our breath is stifled once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And when our wings grow weary of blood, if we must repeat the process; and if it is not very painful, if we must inflict the wound once more, and if the pain persists, even if the wound is perceived to be pierced through and through
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and tough hair, and who have many pores, that you order the loosening of the knots of fat by applying a purgative and dissolving oil
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	or almond oil or sweet pumpkin seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it be in summer, of olive oil of cresson, or of rue, or of chamomile, or some similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is great and cold, if take oil of marigold, or balsam, or oil of ivy, and the like.</start_of_turn>
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if it has to be kept tight and large pores, do not put any oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but must wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or elderberry water, or gourd water, or earthenware water, or some similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or from a surge of mint, and thyme, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And he who has thick saliva rises from wine old, or from a surge of sage, or from an infusion of fennel or chamomile, or from other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and does not feel well from the wind before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and does not sleep after the ventosation,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and must be warned when he must be ventosated and when he is ventosated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And keep him calm who is feverish, and if he is too excited and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is possible that he grasps cold things, such as grapes, onions, lettuce and similar things.</start_of_turn>
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	give him medical food, and mustard poultices, and moist meats.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	and the one who has a cold complexion, let him take honey syrup, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat sparingly, and eat medical foods and small oils and herbs.</start_of_turn
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And when it is windy, if it must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and must give water to others neither before nor after the wind, for the comfort of the principal limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	except that which is sufficient for them, for the rest must abstain from drinking
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The winds that are put to the wound are those that are put on the liver, and on the heel, and under the foot, and on the belly and the belly-button and the groin and the hip, for these members do not suffer from wounds above these.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And it is done only to draw blood from limb to limb.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	And if we put our hands on the limbs when they do not bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as if we put sponges on the belly and the buttocks to reduce the limb.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieve the pain, when there is an operation or a stone, for by its attractive virtue it pulls out the operation, or expels the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so do we do when we put it on the liver and the wrist when there is retained moisture.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these compresses are administered empty with vinegar so simply; and never are they administered together with fire, and never full of cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	if indeed in diseases of the chest, and in such a way that we fill the compress with hot water soon, or with water or where there are herbs covering it that are convenient for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the compress administered with fire is thus:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And has two palms in width and half a palm in depth, and has or costs at the center almost a mile wide, as for to push out an arrow.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And if it is from the start, sweat before if she does not bleed the patient when putting it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is in the middle a stick of iron or wood, to put a bandage in place,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there are great and small according to the ailments and the extent of these things that take them
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the swellings of the limbs are different from those of the veins, and the lean from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And must one place this ventouse upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	then take hold of the collar of silk or linen, and put it into the ventouse through the hole which is in the ventouse.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	if the blood vessel is closed at the bottom of the ventouse, it will not burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it upon the limb, and you must be above the opening which we have mentioned, so that if we see that there is vapor, we can remove the ventouse;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take hold of the limb as before, and begin again if you have mastered it.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	And when it is administered in a pleural disease, at all times, there is no vein or perforation, and it is only administered when it is plain water, and is put on the limb only so little.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	There are no veins in the limbs or parts where one can put a ventouse due to their small size, such as the liver and gums, and similar things.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And in their armpits stripped of hair, whether due to pain or not, and other things similar.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And if the patient testifies that whenever he has tried without pain that the wounds which are in soft and smooth tissue do not feel the slightest discomfort, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in warm water, until they are limp, and do not have anything in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then either bandage the wound and apply a suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the bandages.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	When they are full-grown, and shiny, if it be possible to apply a suction cup, apply it, for this is worth more.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, if you can easily lift the limb, then wring it out, wring it well, and then press it;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb still bleeds too much afterwards, soak it in cold water, and put on, until the wound is healed;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wound is multiplied, put on broken glass or bandages, and similar things, until it is healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or thou takest out half of the hairs of the beard, and leavest them until they are burned at the root, if thou doest stop them now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	or thou takest out half of the hairs of the beard, and leavest them until they are burned at the root, if thou doest stop them now,
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	and if the hairs do not come out easily, rub the root with fresh blood, or insert a needle into it until it comes out.</start_of_turn
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, if they are burned;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	When you see that they are chattering, if powder is poured over an aloe plant and a piece of charcoal is added, or ash, they will now growl.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This marks the beginning of the book of broken bones.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Listen well, my son, for in this book there are no former tales or letters to be found;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	I know of nothing, save by the learning from ancient books, or because I have studied it so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made it clear the forms of the instruments which are brought into play, as I have done in the previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary, therefore, that our words or prologue of this book should be an image of the truth and the chapters or lessons should place their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are proved right learn and master this noble art, and learn it from others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that whenever a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if you must hasten to restore the patient to health from either side, without doing anything else, if there is weakness of the limbs, or youthfulness, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if his tension is not very strong, or too cold; and eat only cold juices, such as barley and oatmeal, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat, until you are certain that the patient has overcome the immediate danger of infection, and that the swelling has subsided from the limb; for if he returns to normal so soon, it is because he has recovered from the first attack.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the fractured bone begins to heal, if you must restore the patient, do not nourish the patient with meats that cause great swelling, or that have viscosity, such as wheat germ in water, and pork, and testicles, and spleen, and veins, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For in part nourishment returns muscle and more quickly the fracture breaks.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Beware that broken bones of bones and cartilages do not mend well without moisture, and that those which are too brittle, such as bones of small intestines, do not join together properly.</start_of_turn>
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, hold tight to the broken bone, that is to say, strong bands which are apt to bind the limb together, until it is firm as before; and do not move it in any way, for because of this you must nourish the limb with solid food, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.</start_of_turn
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by bending, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a whole small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at the shoulder blade there is its engine, and its own instrument in restoring it, according to what is remembered from its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the fracture of the bone is twisted by this that it is twisted well by pushing, and by the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no dislocation there is no great pain, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have dislocation, or fracture, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not possible to move the limb by hand, but medicines come after, then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	If the fracture breaks through to the marrow, and these are the two parts of the joint, it is necessary to hold them now in perfect alignment, even as the abscesses remain in life;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses appear, if you leave them whole, as long as the abscesses are calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it firmly, if possible, and be gentle and sure, and if there are fractures, restore them more easily than if there are pieces; and then hold it firmly once more
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they extend over .ij. parts, if it is the hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or over .ij. cords, or over a cord and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are relieved, if you leave them with all their ligaments attached to the bone as you must, and keep that in your work there comes no injury or pain to the patient.</start_of_turn>
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and stabilize well the joints of the bones according to the best forms.</start_of_turn>
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If he feels well in the hand, though he seems unwell: if the swelling is beautiful and does not tighten too much, do not press as they do who make it come by their work at the height of swelling and contraction of the limb.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	When the limb is stiff, if the patient is groaning in pain that he cannot move, neither awake nor asleep, neither turning nor otherwise;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	take care that the limb is so secure that he does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you must put him in a position where he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him firmly in place, so that no discomfort arises when you restore it
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and tell him how to brace the limb as I shall instruct you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The limb is braced in various ways in small and large sizes and shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thighs and the like: if you cover them with linen cloth which is soft and subtle;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And if those which are large, such as buttocks and legs: if you cover them with a wide and hard cloth, for the large cloths embrace the whole great limb and constrain it everywhere equally, so that there is no tension;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then you must tie on tight stockings, that is two or three according to the size of the limb, and constrain your hand one inch from the top of the wound and loosen the pressure, so that the wound is released one inch from the pressure;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb somewhat, so that you take a great part of the limb back, and then take back another limb, and bind tightly around the wound again.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then raise to the lower part of the break, and hold moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said earlier.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the broken ends some strips of linen or cloth, until they are all even, and then bind all around with thread, and then put your pins well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, if put above soothing things for the abscess, which will stop the swelling, and leave it untouched for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your pins, and let them be about half the width of a broad needle of sage, or of a twig from which we make nails, or of barley straws, and let them be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that when one puts the brace upon the fracture, it should be larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it is necessary for the limb, whether it is small or large
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then is strained upon the bones as you did at the first hour, and then bind under a thread or bandage, as in the first hour upon the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	more is strained is under, rather less; and it is necessary that the thread be medium, not too thick or too thin, and be of linen soft.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	Car si les fils sont gros, si comme j’ai voulu des œuvres des foules qui font leur liéure des cordes de linement tort, c’est un grand erreur, car la liéure ne peut être égale si elle est trop subtilde, et ne convient que s’il y a entre les chevilles une étoile moins de dou.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is nauseated by the nails after stripping in the flesh, if you put down nails of linen or coarse cloth, it will not stain.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the nerve is fractured, I will speak of the cure later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	The wounds that it is not possible to restrain with the hands must be grasped from the toes of the limbs which break first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	When the limb is large, it is not possible to put the supports in place except after five or seven days, or more according to the severity of the wound which comes out;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and when the old wound has healed, to restore the fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some fine flour that sticks to the millstones, and mix it with an abundance of eggs, and make this confection, not too thick or too thin, and use it
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and almond and saffron and gum arabic and mugwort, all in the amount of three; mirra and aloe, in the amount of three; beeswax, eight in the amount of three; and grind them up, and mix them with an abundance of eggs; if the colour of the patient is hot, use this dressing, for it is of good composition, and restores the broken bones immediately, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Other methods of displacement that are worth considering are: mugat and vismalve, with 10 drops each; myrrh and aloes, with 78 drops each; acaice with 5 drops each; arnica with 10 drops each, and grind well, and mix with water or a lot of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other methods of displacement for joints and bones that are loosened from their sockets, and relieve pain that comes from there, and that breaks down bone, and fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and hold it on the area. These plasters do not restore health, but they are good for soothing post-traumatic swelling, and properly relieve pain.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other methods of displacement that restore fractured bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial pavol leaves, grind them together, and make plaster.</start_of_turn>
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of supporting the restoration of a broken bone is to soften the remaining abscess. Take root of chamomile, camomile flowers, violets flowers, wheat flour, and one part of chaff; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander or vinegar and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of support that is more forceful than the first, when the abscess becomes firm during restoration of the limb. Take root of chamomile, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, violets flowers and chamomile flowers, all of which make up one part; grind and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the temperature of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore force except for some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between soft and firm.</start_of_turn>
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen says we must put something warm on the affected limb to restore it, such as mustard, aloe, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of dressing that is useful for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poppy seeds, and vinegar, and mix them evenly, and bruise them, and make a poultice from them.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then take hold of the limb afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that their bones are not fractured; if you do not take hold by hand for a while.</start_of_turn
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sensation of rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen the bandage, and support the limb in place now; and take a lighter drapeil, and a sponge of salt moistened, plunge into water, and raise up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soak in water or rose oil, and bind up with a nut, until you are sure of the healing of the cautery
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and rest the inflammation of the limb, and if the pain persists, then renew the bandage, and a little support, and do not bind too tightly; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is swollen, red, painful, and inflamed throughout, and that it persists despite initial treatment, you must repeat the procedure as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	If it does not yield in the limb what we have said, if it does not yield after two, three, five, or seven days; do not leave it for twenty days, as is seen, until the inflammation has subsided, and approach the conclusion of the disease near its end.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore, restrain it more than before, and fatten its flesh, as I said before; and if you see its flesh dry out more than usual, do not attempt to bring in nourishment;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	The fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	When the work of this chapter is done, cut the nourishment from the limb; and immediately restore what the fools have made, for this is bad, and if there is any suspicion of fear, I see nothing better than to leave it alone and treat it directly.</start_of_turn>
des diverses manieres de brisure	various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many methods of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone snaps all the way down to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as if made by a chip or a twist; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the spear pierces the bone in a reverse direction, and this kind of fracture is called an "absolue"; and the wound of these fractures is great or small
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or snap of a bone, or fracture of the bone above the joint, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst wound, which approaches the gut that is below the bone, or it is on the bone, and is this wound great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is sutured to the bone as closely as a nail, and the wound is small, it is called a "caputla".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made or pierced by a nail, or by a thorn, or by anything similar, and brings the piece of bone inwards, and the limb is bent as when one boils pots when they are over a fire; if between the bone ends.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this has more under it those who have or have had wet bones, as children;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are many such instances of fractures where small pieces are loosened from each other as with these; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all kinds of fractures due to the separation above them, the tension at the edges, and the corrupt marrow that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The blood vessels are recognized by this: when one discovers a bone, and wipes over it, if the black fracture is open
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, take care of the patient’s condition, and if you see no other mishap, like vomiting of bile, emission of urine, extension, and paleness, fever and swelling, and other similar things, if not, it is certain that the matter will not recover without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if no sudden accident befalls thee, and thou hopeth for health, if so, commence the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling comes first to thee, and it be in the armpit, if so, know that it is necessary to remove the bone from the quadrant above the muscle which thou dost touch.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it be in this state, if thou hast haste to remove the bone from the seventh quadrant above the bone, thereby that the bone of the armpit be corrupted, and comes the accident which we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the part which covers the brain, if so, know that thou must make an opening in the wound: and that thou graspest the head of the patient and uncover the bone in every way that thou canst, and on the figure of the wound more rough than thou canst.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if discharge of blood comes from uncovering the bone, or from an abscess, he should assist with what he can; and that you fill the wound with cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And rest the wound until the abscess is calmed; and be sure there is no further discharge of blood. Then begin to close the wound by stitching, and that is done in two ways: one way if the tail of the wound is narrow in front, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another tail that is larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have various sizes of wounds, some wide and some narrow, pointed or blunt, and over a wound that is slight, do not close the wound.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, if you must pierce through, even if you administer wounds with sponges, do not make them larger than necessary, and must have above the point a margin or circle, which must not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these, so that when the flesh comes to the thickness of the bone, if you have sponges throughout, it will fill up the space of the bone. This is the form of the two methods of sponges:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.
