The quality for piercing through a brittle bone is that you put on a sponge on the bone, and turn your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put on another sponge in another place a little later, and do all around, and close as the incisors close the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any instruments that you have as if you were holding tweezers; and keep your hand away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and treated, if it is possible, restore the socket which has been loosened from the bone to all other instruments which are like an incisor, but it is necessary that it should be more firm and subtle than the other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it remains loose of all the small bones, neither nails, if the bone is slightly injured by instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and sponges as we have said
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is like the Galicians say, which is more moist; and the load is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, either the fracture that appears swollen, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and grasp the handle of this incisor lens, for this is its form.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut too deeply from one side, for the soft parts are in the marrow, if you cut too deep towards the bone; then hold a little mallet above, so that you can gently break the bone all around, and take care of the cloth that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is near the bone, if the bone is slightly broken, for we must break the bone quite steadily, without fear or pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks but does not pierce the skin, cut the bone only slightly above; there are small pieces remaining. If you can repair the fracture, remove the sharp fragments with blunt instruments of various sizes, in order to close as many cavities as possible, according to the work and the appearance of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are large fragments remaining, and after further bluntness, and it does not stop, continue to do so until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	Concerning other small wounds and fractures, it is necessary to provide the remedy according to its location; and this is something that is not mentioned by him who has studied this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is discovered, take one drape of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another drape of linen doubled in half or in quarters, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you wish, that you do not tear the wound, then administer further linen, and do not restrain it more than is necessary for just holding the wound in place.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and leave it thus for a while or two, until the swelling of the wound has subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of iris, barley flour, and incense powder, and an ointment; from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer appropriate medicines without biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And beware that the wound is well closed, that you do not leave it open, neither do you leave it half-closed, for when it is closed upon the brain, if it bursts and swells, it brings great harm to the patient; for when one puts on top of it something biting, if it does not desist from below.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other force comes from the medicine we have put on, that some good may result from it, if you take a part of honey, and two parts of rose oil and glue one with the other; and put it on the wound
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the treatment in the manner of treatment that is suitable, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then comes the treatment in the manner of treatment that is suitable, as long as it is sane.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the three parts is broken, if it is recommended that you bite your little toe or hole in the neck, and put the break of that bone inside your index finger and the heel together, until it returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do it gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is on the upper part of the limb, and it cannot be reached from below, it is proper that you place it even with the head of a splint as wide as a thumb.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is high up, if you do it again, and you are delaying the restoration of the limb, if you wish;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	then after the seventh or the tenth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then you must bind the limb tightly at the top of the fracture
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or if you must bind it elsewhere, if the fracture is there; and let the attempts be so great that they fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say no restorer shall moisten the tents in the burrow, and die each one for himself. It seems good to me, but it is necessary that they be moistened in the composition of an egg yolk and meal powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never again shall one put goose feathers instead of tents, and if indeed there is snow hanging overhead, and the wind blows, and blows the patient among; or do as you please.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if someone’s clothes come to the neck while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil, or some potage of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if after the application of the poultice there is no relief, if you put on a plaster of boiled linseed meal, fine powder of incense, confirmed with the yolk of an egg, then put on light covers, and do not bind tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	If the swelling is slight and is broken into small pieces, if you have suitable instruments, then extract the fragments, close the wound, and treat with poultices and ointments that are useful in such cases.</start_of_turn>
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no pus in the wound, if you can cure it with stitches, and put on ointment, as long as it is healing.</start_of_turn>
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the route of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without injury to the surrounding tissues, and the fracture is slight, and not deeply fractured, except for the teeth which must be loosened gently.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is appropriate, if the fracture is in the distal part, to bite down on the index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take the index finger of the right hand, and touch the fracture gently, and hold it steady with the other hand in turn, and make it equal
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if it is recommended that you administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth arises, or swelling, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken jaw cerote on the jaw and put on a double drape; and on the drape place a large well-made patty, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it to the tooth that you wish, and command the patient to rest, and feed on soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, if it comes loose at the root, and then return to its place; put on a plaster on it, with coarse powder of almonds with abundant eggs or oatmeal, after you have set the cerote; and put on a soft bandage, and if the plaster comes loose, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it heals; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a wound comes out, if it threatens what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, heal so that no part of the bone is left bony; if subtle of the bone has instruments covering it.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, if it has flared up as you need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have sutured all these pieces, and there is no more bleeding, if the wound is wide, and put on some covering materials that cover the wound, to absorb moisture, until it is healed
de la forcele	and strong.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two ways: either it is broken and loosened in three parts, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	When the break is in line with the wound, have two assistants; one should hold the limb that feels the force of the break; and the other should extend the neck towards the part; then put the break back in place so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither bulge nor swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend it further, put under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of lead, or cloth, as thick as you need; and extend and keep the forcele, and strain the lead at your hand, so that you can put the break back in place as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to manage the head of the shoulder when it comes out of its place, because it will slip downwards, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his heel, and put the shoulder in its place, that is, the middle ear, and hold the minister in the lower part of the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, know that you must cut there; and extract the fragments gently, and if the bone will not join together by any means, if the socket has been damaged at one of your incisors, but that you put in place the shoulder instrument to protect the face.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and seems like a scoop, and is not crooked, and is as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and has two holes, as you can see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bone.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are assured of the depth of the wound, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the depth, if you employ the wound with draping and bandages, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the wound has become infected, if there is moisture, let draping with oil of roses, and balsam, and wine, and put on it.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The hardening of the bone, when it is painful and swollen, is that you put on the bone the plaster of fine flour and eggshell, and put on it light bandages, and put a sponge soaked in oil under the wound, if necessary.</start_of_turn
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very great bend of a palm of broad size, and put two layers of drape on the toes, and hold them in place; then take a subtle wedge of two fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bundle, so that the head of the bundle remains suspended.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Put the wedge on the bulge, and turn the bundle towards the collarbone, and drain the inner skin, and drain the outer skin; and hold the outer skin taut, and when you see that the ligature holds the bulge steadily, and you clearly see that the wedge does not move from the broken bone, if you reward each jerk, and when you see that the limb is relaxed;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put under his buttock one small cushion to support the limb; if you align the fracture of the scapula with the displacement of the shoulder blade, or if you bind the arm to the collarbone, and do not loosen it until it is quite well healed, for about twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the displacement, if you see that there is need for it, and hold and leave it alone until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than most men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then restart the dislocation, if you see that there is need for it, and hold and leave it alone until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time than most men.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder is fractured or dislocated and does not spontaneously reduce, force must be used; if the limb is repositioned according to the fracture figure, and is held in its natural position in all positions; then put on coarse powder of mill with plenty of eggshell, and apply a bandage, and put on a broad splint wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is fixed in no part of the shoulder, use the suspension of linen thread, so that the splint rests evenly; and then restrain with a strong belt that the splint does not move, and look at the limb every hour; and every time that it moves, if you restrain it, and put back the splint if it has been forced out of place, and keep the patient lying down; and the shoulder is restored in about twenty or twenty-five days. And when that number is completed, if the limb is loosened, and the patient is able to walk, for it is not the bone that is easily fractured.

de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone sticks forward, and does not yield at all, if it remains in place, and the bone, do as we have said concerning the breaking of the forcele to appease the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this often happens; but it often breaks with a sudden movement. And when it is broken in the middle, if it is displaced, and the patient feels great pain, and loss of appetite, vomiting, and even vomiting blood, and opens the wound in the broken bone, and all that.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient lies still on his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and subtly make them even in all positions until the limb is restored to its normal shape; then put on splints and bandage with fine salt or other soft material, and cover with a cloth, and bind firmly over the broken bone, if it does not move; and turn the limb around the back and strain it gently, and award some time the limb, and if it relaxes, strain it again; and if it comes loose again, because of corrosion or inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are hasty, loosen it and remove the splint, and address the cause of the fracture; then restore the splint and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	And if the patient lies still on his back, put one cushion between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulder blades and unite the edges of the ribs with your hands, and subtly make them even in all positions until the limb is restored to its normal shape; then put on splints and bandage with fine salt or other soft material, and cover with a cloth, and bind firmly over the broken bone, if it does not move; and turn the limb around the back and strain it gently, and award some time the limb, and if it relaxes, strain it again; and if it comes loose again, because of corrosion or inflammation that comes from the bone, or pain or swelling, if you are hasty, loosen it and remove the splint, and address the cause of the fracture; then restore the splint and strain it until it is healed.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fracture of the bones only comes from great pains after the back, and at the head of the shoulder, and they do not happen for anything else except that they are slippery; and the patient often feels them at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And if the restoration is such that you make equal the fracture, as it should be. Then put in place the dressing, and bind with an awl, if you must.

And if the fracture of the ribs is declining inwards, if the patient feels great pain, and swelling, like with pleurasy, because the bone touches the gut; and there are pains, and vomiting, and vomiting of great quantity of blood, this is a grievous disease, and they have put great pain on it.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if these things are said, it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push out the fracture outwards.</start_of_turn>
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except in the case of ulcers that do not heal, when they have not appeared.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have appeared, if they are healthy.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one puts a bandage on the limb because of its swelling; for this is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the excess moisture from the limb because of the weakness of its position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to keep the wound even, then either cure with a pleurisin dressing, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the patient experiences great pain that they cannot bear from the bone that points to the navel, and there is doubt, then it is permitted to make an incision above the broken rib and insert instruments to hold the liver in place. Then one must pierce the bone, treat it lightly, and then sew up the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with sponges. If an abscess comes up, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil over it and hold the liver in place. Cure until the liver returns to its normal position, or until the rib is healed.
de la brisure dou col	If the rib is fractured,
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	The rib is often fractured along with the collarbone, and often blood flows; and the spine is also affected
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to no avail, and you know not whether he will recover or not, if you take warning if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and that they cannot be moved or extended, and when you prick them with a needle, if he does not feel it. Such is the death of many cases, and if you move them and he feels well when they are strained and pointed, such is the sign that the bone joint is saved, and the patient will recover, if we put treatment to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if something like this comes to the heel of the back, and you know not whether it will recover or not, if you take warning if the heel is softened and the accident is there which is in the hands and on the back there is an excessive swelling and emission of matter; and when it is squeezed on the belly, there is an excessive emission of matter. And when it is squeezed on the back and he sees blood, if he cannot bear it. Such is the death of many: if he does not work in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen, if the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is an abscess, if you prick it with a needle, put on rose oil or oil of rue marigold, until it is calmed; then put on one of the soothing and drying patches, and bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if a bone breaks, if you must cover on the limb; and unite the fragments of the wound, if it is large, with a bandage, then cure with oil that fills the wound, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is fractured, which is called the «fracture of the marrow», if it is on the outside of your left hand, and put it equal to the other hand on your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need them; then strain it, and if there are broken bones underneath, if you leave it there, and unite the bones, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	and the fracture of the thigh bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, if there is no other injury to the head; and if so, it is long and hangs down, and causes the patient pain in the limb, swelling, and bending of that which is fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the fracture is at the head of the thigh bone, extend your hand over the fracture as long as you are over the break; and hold the limb in such a way as to reduce the fracture and restore its natural position. If the fracture is only at the head, leave it in its natural position.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or downward, make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of the fracture is complete.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you place them on the shoulder, then put on a staff of wood or bone, and hold the brace still, so that it does not move; and use the weight of the limb to stretch the ribs, as long as the limb is flexible.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swelling comes, if it does not subside, until the swelling subsides, put on what we have mentioned before; and then rest, and stretch if it is convenient, without any mishap; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And thus make two incisions on the shoulder, and draw out the bone upwards, and hold the patient above a seat; then gently bend the arm down towards the elbow, with a curve of the arm, then place something heavy on the fist, or the minister extends the arm backwards; then put the eyes level with the hand clasped, until the dislocation returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is if you support the patient on his shoulder, and bind the arm to his collar, and order the attendants that one holds what is above the dislocation at his hands, and the other holds the shoulder bones apart, and stretch the skin outwards.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is too strong, if it tightens [the limb], let the bones of the briseure break; and over the briseure, extend thumbs of the attendants at their side. And if the briseure is close to the head of the shoulder, if you can put [a support] between the bone of the armpit and the other towards the shoulder, break the briseure; and if the briseure is towards the shoulder, if you can put [a support] lightly, cautiously, as long as the briseure is equal on both sides, then put it equal, if possible, and tighten, because if you do not tighten, the wound will not close.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the wound does not close, if it does not tighten by itself, put on moist linen and rose oil until the wound is calmed; then tighten, and the manner of tightening is that you put the support on the briseure, then assemble the limb on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put the bandage, and tighten on the support and the limb, so that the limb is steady, without anything hindering it, or without moving the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, if you use pins, put on the briseure a pin that is wider and stronger than the others, and put between the thumbs of two pins as much space as the thickness of two pins; then tighten on the pins, as I have said above concerning the chapter on the briseure, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling of the limb, and the tightening, as we have said, in the meantime that you restore the limb, and you doubt the abscess is closed, if you leave it to join up until seven days, as we have said; then look carefully for two days, that swelling does not increase or arise in the limb, or that the swelling does not return to the limb because it is too tight. If the swelling persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such thing happens, if two or more days have passed, and the patient lies down on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put a compress of coarse wool equally over the limb, and look for an hour or two, whether the limb is straightened out, or whether the ligaments are softened; if the swelling persists, by the power of medicine, and do the flesh that we have in front of us, in part as much as the flesh is at the first tension; and when it starts to recover, if it is large. And it is customary that the bandage and the limb should be taken off in forty days; and then it should be loosened and bathed, and given other medicines for the limb to recover. And if the swelling is tight and engorged, if it should be loosened for a day or two.
de la brisure du bras	... of the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna". The former is small and is that which supports the pouch [of muscle]; the latter is large and is that which is bowed, towards the little finger. By chance the large radius alone breaks, or the small, and by chance both together break.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone breaks, the restoration is slight and the healing; but when the large bone breaks, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when they break together. If only the small bone breaks, if the limb is slightly extended, and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that breaks, if the limb is strained more strongly; and is extended over the thumb, and keeps the pouch of the hand higher than the other, and the small bone is lower than the others, and the patient's hand is crossed over itself, with the thumb in front, than the patient suffers no pain; then extend the forearm at the wrist towards the hand or towards the little finger, and one hand towards the other at the elbow. And then put the limb in its proper position, as well as possible
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If it breaks into pieces, if you put some back into its place, and if there is none that prick at its root as before, you will not be able to restore it to its place, even if you leave it alone like we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the fracture there is a wound, as I have mentioned in the singular case; take the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	If at the commencement of restoration comes out abscesses, if you glue [it], that is, drape it with gauze made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is neither too tough nor too soft; and bind it so that it is firm but not too tight. And then bone the wound and put in place the dressing of fine meal with a great deal of eggshell, for put the stars in, and make the fracture solid again, and a space wider than the others; and the stitches must be of such a size as to fill the gap. There must be more stars about the fracture than elsewhere; and it is strained more on the fracture than elsewhere, and all the days less in aligning, as I have said at the commencement of this chapter; and let the bandages be soft and moist on the fracture, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread that is used be neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And rest the limb and the limblet after a few days.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If other evils follow the limb, as if with itching that comes with the limb, then you must know that you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching is calmed; and then leave the limb still. And then restart the treatment, and when the flesh is softened and the bone is loosened, and like similar things, if necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the swelling does not return to the limb, because it is too tight, then you must soften it, indeed, and leave it alone for a while, until the swelling goes down, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of these things that we have said help the patient, if not until about twenty days, then put his hands to his collar, and keep his collar even, and take care of movement and eating, and sleep on his back; and give him food every three days, or every four days, according to the composition and complexion of the medicines.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	From the breaking of the hand
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	When the hand is broken or wet, if it is known that the patient will travel, let the patient sit comfortably facing forward; then put the hand on a wide bandage, and stretch the broken bones evenly; put the bones back in their place, as well as possible; put on the plaster and bandage, if necessary; and if there is a wound, put on a bandage according to the amount of bleeding; and be covered with one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	When the fracture is in the armpit towards the belly of the limb, make a loop of bandage, and order the patient to grasp their broken limb; then tighten with a long bandage, and put on a collar as wide as the limb, and tighten it as much as it is convenient.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the wrist, if you must know, put a splint above and one below in the palm, so that the thumb is over and straight, then bind it all around the wrist, and seal the loop between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to neither of us, if it is at the elbow, if you must know; put it even, if it is necessary; and strain it with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right-angle splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, if like in the index or one of the others, if you must put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding firmly, as much as is useful, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the burn, and cure what comes with it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	And if the break comes to neither of us, if it is at the elbow, if you must know; put it even, if it is necessary; and strain it with the palm, and if you see that you must put a right-angle splint to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is in another place, if like in the index or one of the others, if you must put it even, and bind it with the two fingers that follow; or you bind them all together, holding firmly, as much as is useful, or you put on a splint, as for a pouch; and take care in the restoration and in the arrangement of the burn, and cure what comes with it, as I have said.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound with a thread above the fracture and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, and extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is embedded in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the groin, if either the upper ligament tears near the navel, or the lower ligament near the fracture. And if it is close to the knee, and either the upper ligament near the knee, or the lower extension; then put the thumbs of the hands together until the bone is restored to its natural position, and then put on the dressing and bind it, without causing further damage.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess above, if you leave it calm and return to your work and your cure; the ligature is made in part for that.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	If there is an abscess above, if you leave it calm and return to your work and your cure; the ligature is made in part for that. It is necessary to wrap the limb with a strong bandage, such as linen doubled over twice or thrice, and to keep the excess tension, then to bend the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and to pass a thread long between the heel and the limb, leaving the bandage loose at the ankle, and to pass the thread over the limb and over the heel, and to place a button on the limb and on the heel, and to put on the bandage around the abscess, and to put on a button on the bone of the limb; and to use the remaining thread between the limb and the heel of cloth so that it is even, and to begin to tie in pairs or threes on the abscess; and the more you go up on the abscess, the less the strain; and when you have passed three threads that you had passed between the limb and the heel, and having tied two buttons that are below, then to return to the ankle at the level of the thread, as long as you see that the pain has gone away.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If there is a loosening, if it comes loose, and if you address what has come; as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that prick, if it is necessary, it is to cauterize; if not, it is necessary to cut the vein, and drain away; and to cure as we have said, as long as it is necessary.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this case when it is set with sticks, as in the arm or the leg; however, in the restoration made in this case, I do not feel pain in the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And so, if the bone is reset in one day, or less or more, according to the diversity of temperaments.</start_of_turn>
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin street.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	In the groin street there is often breakage, but it often rains many times. And if it breaks, it is no longer just a tear, or a perforation, but there is great pain, and this is well known.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the restoration is done, if you put everything round back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly, put the bandage on, and put on a round cushion, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the instructions that we have said before, as in incision and other things; if you put into each accident what it should be put in, as long as it is sound.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if the restoration is done, if you put everything round back in its place, as long as it is put together firmly, put the bandage on, and put on a round cushion, if you have need of it, and strain it as it should be strained; then reward all the instructions that we have said before, as in incision and other things; if you put into each accident what it should be put in, as long as it is sound. And finish the fracture of the limb.
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	And finish the fracture of the limb. The bones in the limb are two: one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "facet"; and both are fractured as it happens in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm, and the work is all done in one.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if two bones are fractured together, the limb is twisted from every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a bone is fractured in two, the limb is twisted from the front.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if a large bone is fractured, it causes great pain, and one can see it well; and it is twisted about. Therefore, bring extension, and set it even, and bind the limb even; but take note, if the fracture is severe, and there are many pieces, that the extension should be less severe and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take four strips of coarse gauze that will cover the limb from one end to the other, and bind them around the limb from the knee to the toes; then cover with four layers of bandage, and bind firmly in the middle, and do not allow the limb to bend to the right or to the left, and it is well done; and no one should administer anything that is long along the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is of many pieces, that the extension should be less severe and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of bone fractures which are painful.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but in the bones of the limb there is no fracture at all, and two must suffice; and there is no other reason except for fear of death.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the limb, and you see these bones pressing against one another, if you put the limb so that it hangs in the air, as if it were flying away, and then put your limb back on the ground, where the bones were lifted up, then press on them until they return to their place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put on a small bandage to the belly of the limb, then bind the limb steadily, and when you have bound it up, cover it with a cloth, and other things as you deem necessary
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if you loosen the dressing, because you will find the bones equal, whether they are fractured or displaced.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there be two fractures, if you restore them as we have said, do so with two hands; then set a splint according to the length of the two bones, and make it wider than the former; then put on the dressing that I have mentioned. If there are three or more fractures, break them; and set upon each bone a splint according to its quantity, covered with a layer of linen, and strain the dressing down onto the bones.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have mentioned concerning other fractures, as we have said; and secure each accident as it should be secured.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the thumb bone.</start_of_turn>
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, if she sits enlarged, then lean her forward; and hold her back by the back; then fill the belly with cotton, and put as much in as a stone; then pull out the woman, and keep her back and front; and then jump the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the belly, and return the bone with the stone; and when she has seen a pee, if the stone is in the cotton, and when she has peed, she will be restored; so be it for thirty days or more: if the fracture is restored, and if you see it, take a bladder of aloe and bind it to the belly with a bandage, and pour all the bladder into the belly; then blow into the bandage, until the bladder is expelled: the belly will then return to its normal state.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	When the forearm bone of a man is broken, or of a woman, if you restore it as we have said concerning the thigh bone; and these fractures which are not obvious proceed from those who put their study and practice into them, and who read my book. For the fracture signifies in more ways the right way of restoration: therefore take heed.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the limb, when it is broken, take a gooseberry and put it in the limb; then cover it with cloth, and leave it for two days or until it is healed, and it will be healed completely.
de brisure avec plaie	From the break with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as if it were the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or similar, that it be set now, as the pain that we have mentioned testifies.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well healed, if there is only a stain of vitriol, if you have nothing else, then resume the fracture in this way, or in that way, as soon as possible, for if there is no further displacement, the fracture will heal on its own.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there is displacement of the bone, if you leave the fracture undisturbed until the swelling subsides, as long as the displacement is not too great, and do not touch the bone or the surrounding tissue, for you will risk causing further damage.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks are apparent on the surface like a discovered wound, then you must know that you must press them lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the swelling does not appear to be pressing equally with your hands, if there is this instrument of iron which is about thirteen or fourteen inches long, and the breadth is according to the quantity of the wound; for this reason it must be applied with three or four fingers, as much as is necessary in the case of a wound of breaking. And let it be round and thick, so that it does not press too much on the limb during your work, and let it be before and thick in front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	It is called "palainche" because it must be known that when the limb is curved it must be placed on the head of the apparent bone; and once it has been placed, when it comes back, let the one be equal to the other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, if you must cope with the head of the bone, as long as the instrument has possession of it
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a covered instrument that can reach the area, or if you pierce or draw out, from that point forward remove whatever is remaining embedded in the bone, rough or soft scraps.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	When the bone is restored and the patient experiences great pain afterward, swelling that it is not in its natural position. If you do more than that, then moisten it i.e. cover with black vinegar, and keep it like that; and do not put any cerate or other thing on the wound, because it will cause putrefaction and corruption. Then give the patient stars when the bone has been restored, and leave the wound uncovered, and keep the covering close to the wound according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times this has happened to fools, and it has caused the patient to die or to become paralyzed or to decay on numerous occasions; or the inflammation is more mild and soft than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that any remedy will help, as we have said, and you find pain in the limb, if it does not suffice to put on stars; but cover loosely, instead of stars, with coarse cloth, and bind them. And when you see afterwards i.e. a little or a lot of blood draining from the wound, if that which you put on the whole time has not worked, put ointment healing wounds, like ointment tetrafarmaçon and the like.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be immobilized in part as much as is possible so that it does not bend excessively easily.</start_of_turn>
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the limb persists in its displacement, and it cannot be reduced but returns to its place spontaneously, with small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you reduce the wound with care, and pull out all these broken pieces that cause this pain.</start_of_turn
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if there is a fistula or other corruption of this kind, if it is necessary to cure it, as it is stated in the preceding chapter. And when the bone is broken, and appears on the limb, as the bone of the thigh or the shoulder, and other large bones, if it is not treated, for in many cases there is loss of life, but let it alone until it has healed; by chance it will disappear after twenty or thirty days, and then cure the wound if you wish; or leave it alone.</start_of_turn
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From the beard which comes out from the beard hair.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	From the beard which comes out from the beard hair. Many times after the heat of the wind comes out of the joint, even when it is close to the limb; and it is a helpful sign to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore that I am warned: if it has been administered stiptic medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollum, acacia, and similar things, that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is stiptic or with abundance of egg or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not move it from hand to hand until it is healed; and then dislocate it, and do it again, until the dislocations are bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of sponge; for the property of sponge is that it solidifies all the swellings under the limb; and if the dislocation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to break it, if the swelling above has burst, and to make the apparent excess; or you leave it without a drain, as long as it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after the bandage
