Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored, and hangs limp and limp after the limb is weak and limp, if there is any cause for it: because it was too tight and did not stretch enough; or because there are too many bands, and they do not permit the limb to move smoothly; or because of excessive bruising; or from too great a movement, not even in its hour; or because there is much blood in the flesh, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient walk, and tighten the limb, until it is strengthened in him; and give him baths, and make him merry and cheerful; then put on a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great nourishment, and the blood often turns red, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and then restore it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the disease.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the limb is deformed, all in vain does it retain its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have had this done in our land; this practice is blamed, and there results great harm, and by chance the death of the patient. However, if the swelling and torture are fresh, if you can raise them with warm water, or soften them with herbs such as elderberry leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and you do make an emollient plaster, as with aquilon well made, and take the nourishment of elderberry, and confit with butter of gelline or olive oil, and make plaster upon; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that alleviate the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And never must the bone be dislocated by continuous rubbing for a long time with wet hands. And keep the limb moving during the hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like a stone, and requires iron tongs, if you cover it just to the bone, make a slight incision; and put cushions and padding in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore its normal position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if it is late, if the limb is swollen, and by chance if it is reset, there will be pain at the root; for this reason one must not move it while it is swollen: many times it causes swelling and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this happens, if the patient recovers the limb, leave it alone until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb high and with oil, then support it slightly, and cure each limb as it comes into its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end of the foot.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	When the jaws are clenched, there are two common dislocations: either they are displaced from their sockets and softened by the muscle; or they are entirely displaced and hang downwards, causing the tongue to hang out of the mouth, unable to close the mouth and swallowing becomes difficult.</start_of_turn>
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will often spontaneously reduce on its own.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accompanied, you must immediately reduce it without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such manner as the minister grasps the head of the patient and supports his gaze with one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is three-quarters gone; and the other hand should be placed against the opposite side, to make them even; and command the patient to soften his jaw and move it from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And his eye should be level, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if the two jaws are together, if they arise with hot water and oil, so that they remain lightly; do not force to return it, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth does well close, soften the sensation by gently pressing; then put on damp cloths in a circle made of rose oil and wax, and bind them lightly with thread.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, and their arms be placed between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, or attempt to stretch, but take hold of something light, as long as the pain persists, and keep the jaws still;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then gently move what they see lightly, and do not work too hard to open the mouth to eat or drink, as long as the jaw is well fixed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws do not manage to be returned to their point at an hour, and are not otherwise converted at their leisure, if thereby fever and customary sickness arise, and by chance solution of the belly, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is a loss; and many times death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot remove from the bone without causing damage, and is useless every time it is attempted, and one can well tell.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And if the patient lies supine on his back, extend his arms; then press the limb towards your palm, and it will return; then put on the dressing and bandage, and restrain it.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head of the shoulder, which is towards the side, cannot be loosened; if it does loosen once, if you leave it in place, as we have said; then put on the dressing and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is well
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the same must be done with the shoulder-blade, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	From the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	The shoulder is dislocated due to two things: firstly, that it is displaced at the glenohumeral joint; and secondly, that it is displaced at the acromioclavicular joint; and by chance it is displaced at the supraspinatus, and this is dangerous.</start_of_turn>
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not slip from the shoulder behind or from front to back; rather it is displaced from the front towards the armpit, just as with those who have a great deal of flesh; or with those who have little flesh, it is displaced at the point of the supraspinatus, and this is dangerous.</start_of_turn
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens that there is a fracture or dislocation, and it inflates the shoulder with a hot abscess, and care must be taken that it is not displaced by this.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is appropriate to translate the text line-by-line:
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	It is appropriate to translate the text line-by-line:
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	It is appropriate to translate the text line-by-line:
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And thus, if it is displaced upwards, if not hidden, for you will find it plainly visible on palpation.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this manner of dislocation is not without force to restore, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician holds the painful limb upwards, then places his thumbs under the armpit, and holds the joint forcefully upwards towards the sky; and the physician holds the limb and extends it upwards, thus if necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said before, if it is necessary, it is to be bathed in warm water; and to be administered soothing and comforting nourishment, such as a decoction of rue, fennel and honey in water, and to be administered.</start_of_turn
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then either soothe the patient on his back, and put on the seat of the assle a cushion of lint equal in size, neither too soft nor too hard, then place his hand on the cushion, and keep the head of the shoulder firmly in place, and handle the hand of the patient.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another assistant must hold the head of the patient firmly, so that it does not move backwards; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and that there is someone present who is greater in size than the patient; and that you put two fingers under the edge of the shoulder, and hold the shoulder up, so that the patient’s arm hangs down.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another minister treats the painful hand that is below the belly. And if the patient is too weak, if he can hold nothing heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And thus we also see in another way: and it is thus that we grasp the testicles in the earth, so that the head of the shoulder may be as round as a ball, neither too big nor too small;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then we must put a soft bandage over the patient’s hand, but that it should not be too tight or too loose; then we must stretch out the hand downwards with the other hand, and the dislocation will return to its place immediately
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return by all these things we have said, do this: take hold of the shoulder with two great hands and three fingers, which has the head bent inwards so that it can enter through the armpit, as in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then he should lie upon the head of the shoulder draped with a cloth, so that the patient does not bleed; and put the hand of the patient behind the shoulder; and extend the arms above the shoulder, and place the shoulder against the arm, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm upon the shoulder blade of a broad shield, and extend the hands downwards, or leave the forearm hanging down from the other side: the dislocation is now corrected.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is corrected, in whatever way it is, if you command that you put behind the shoulder a ball of wool as long as it is even, then put on the shoulder pad with a sprinkle of wheat flour, with incense and alum on the whole shoulder and around, then strain out behind the shoulder immediately, and turn the limb on the shoulder pad, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is commanded that he should move little by little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then move more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is firm and is not softened, if it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is forced out of place by moisture or for some other reason, if you must administer cautery to the second degree, if it is placed before or alongside the cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this, and it loosens after three days, and the joint will not stay in place, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the elbow, and the bones, or behind, if it is made by impulse, and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And if after healing the limb complains by remaining stiff, if the patient uses it many times, while the stiffness gradually subsides, it returns to its former state.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And it must be known that if it is possible to restore it again as before, when it has been pulled out, if it should grieve you to bring it back, for in such a case it cannot be restored altogether, even if it is at the furthest end; it is better that it remains dislocated than to be restored in this way, for it is of more great pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and hold it from the root of the limb that is relaxed.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer great extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and support it with two ministers, if it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder joint, and having enveloped a double-length and wide bandage around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you look at the joint with its hand, if there is no oil on the joint to nourish it, then hold the joint firmly until it recovers;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is healed, put on a dry bandage with eggshell, and extend the arm firmly, and hold the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it there for some days, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, if you notice that it is not properly aligned, repeat the displacement and reinsert the limb, and leave it in that position for some days until it is firmly set; then you can remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If after the joint has been reset, pain persists, and it moves, bathe and massage it thoroughly, and press until the pain subsides; or apply a poultice of mutton fat on the joint, and leave it in place for a day and a night, then extract the bone, and wash it.</start_of_turn>
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	When it sweats, gently dry the joint, then replace the poultice, and then wash or bathe; do this three or four times until it is healed; and if you see that it is still painful, put on a wet cloth soaked in broth and bind it on; if it recovers.</start_of_turn>
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand: the joint of the hand is loosened, and the return is laborious, more than any other joint in the body; it must be immediately repositioned in its place, while it is still loosened, even if the limb is swollen or if there is subsequent displacement.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the repositioning is that you place the painful hand on a table, and extend the limb, and look at it to make it even, so that it puts its palm on the surface of the joint and stretches it until it returns to its normal position
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, you must watch if it is well positioned; then put the painful side of the hand on a table at extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient’s hand face down on the table and their gaze downwards on the joint. If it returns, that is well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If this does not happen, if the strain of calming the spasms subsides, leave the hand in its normal position to resume its place naturally.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it does not bear it, and you do not manage to put it back after a few days, the joint will become stiff.</start_of_turn>
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and do not cause him any further pain, except that which the hands suffer naturally, and do not attempt to extract anything from him: for if the nerves are cut or the veins are broken, nothing will be of any use except to cauterize in this case, and by chance there is nothing else.</start_of_turn
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at rest, if you put on the bandage that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no pain, if there is hot swelling, and you rub it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the arm</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the bones of the hand dislocated at the front or at the back or in the belly;
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	When it is thus, let the limb be held firm, and support the dislocation at its root until it returns to its place; then sustain the head of the limb toward the part where it is joined.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	When it is thus, let the limb be held firm for three days, and then put it even; and do not bind it, as we have said, and do not move it, and bind it again; and do this often, until it is firm.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same in case the dislocation is loose at the shoulder, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same in case it is loose from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Due to the loosening of the scapula from the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the scapula of the back or the neck is loosened, or if there are several loosenings, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in jeopardy.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the sign is that the spurting of blood appears in a contrary direction, it cannot be held, and often mollifies no limb, or the buttocks or arms or legs.</start_of_turn
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the scapula moves three parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbosite."
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The remedy is that if the swelling has arisen from infancy, and no other cure or treatment can be found.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from sitting or blows or similar things, say the old physicians in their great wisdom, or it brings no great benefit;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes before, there is no remedy or treatment.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And thus also, as it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except by that which comes from behind, as I have said.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And thus also, as it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except by that which comes from behind, as I have said. And it is that the patient should keep his face even and relaxed, and hold his breath, because it will not move
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	and thus also, as it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except by that which comes from behind, as I have said. And it is that the patient should keep his face even and relaxed, and hold his breath, because it will not move. Then he should pinch his thumb at the top of the earth forms, and another has feet, and bind a thread around the patient's buttocks, and another has knees, and has ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and thus also, as it comes directly in these costs, and it cannot be cured except by that which comes from behind, as I have said. And it is that the patient should keep his face even and relaxed, and hold his breath, because it will not move. Then two ministers know the threads, one at the top and the other at the feet, among the twelve thumbs.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well closed, as we have said, and look that he puts his palms on the spine, as long as it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a thumb and two fingers of length, and press down on the area, and let the patient lie on his side, and hold the head of the thumb down on the area, and put the middle of the thumb on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and put his eyes on the other head of the thumb, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it does not work, do it at the wrist that is twisting in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	Et est que tu fiches de trois tisons au chef du malaide d’un bras de grand, et devers les pieces trois autres, et ait entre chaque tison, desure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And it is that you must pinch three times at the head of the patient’s arm of great size, and at the pieces three others, and between each pinch, there must be a suture and a bandage, a palm of space of length; and between each of these three pinches must be a turning of the skin, so that the line of the skin turns, and there must be in each turning three small pins of a palm’s length, to return the turning.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then you must join that which is among the armpits to the turning at the head, and the other join to the pieces at the other turning, and the master puts in the pin equal if as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, put upon a dry patch with abundance of oil, and then press, and then support with a tablet of .iij. long, that it may encompass the root of the rib and the part of the spine that is painful, and bind with a thread as we have said, and give the patient nourishment secretly until it is healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if nothing comes to an end of the sickness, it is permitted to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said above; and never is any piece of lead to be administered.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And never does the appearance at the back of the shoulder bone in the back appear, and take care that this is not a dislocation; for it is the bone that opens, for it is not to be presumed: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Dislocations of the shoulder are only caused by dislocations of the shoulder and elbow joints; they do not occur with other joints. The dislocation of the shoulder is destabilized in three parts: front and back, and front and back; the more destabilized it is in front, the more destabilized it is behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And knowledge of this dislocation is that when the limb is joined to the shoulder, if it is longer and the patient’s knee is greater than the normal knee, and the patient cannot double his knee at the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the lesion which is left from the heat of the cautery, because the head of the humerus comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he is well limbed as before; however, do not double his knee joint excessively with pain, and if you see him do so carelessly, do not attempt to stop him beforehand, and retain his urine, and swell his ankle, and when he walks, let him pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he cannot expand his knee, cannot double it, and is that his limb is shorter than the other, and his ankle is softened, and that his shoulder joint is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The head of the shoulder must be reset if an old dislocation persists, and it persists as before; and it is not to be presumed that any treatment will be effective.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty in returning the joint, and stretching it inwards and outwards, and moving it to the right and left; by chance, if it returns, there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, if you must summon one or two strong ministers, and stretch the limb firmly for two or three hands, or for as long as you wish to bind it over the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And another minister extends his hand downwards between his knees, then grasps it with a loop of thread above the hip; and another holds the head of the thread.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	He extends upwards and downwards all at once, as long as the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is often used in this case, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If this is not the case, if you must put the cure in place. When the dislocation is freed, you must place the limb over the patient’s side, and put the loop over the root of the hip, and the limb which is below the ankle, then extend the loop upwards towards the ankle and downwards towards the forcele;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant and embrace the great head of the shoulder of the ailing person, and stretch it out to the side: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is less severe than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you do not manage to hold it in this manner as we have said, if you must, bind the two limbs of the patient together with a strong thread over the two nails and over the two knees, and so extend the limb more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then hang from the head of a staff, or on the ground two arms long; then command one minister to embrace the head of the shoulder, and let another minister hang alongside the patient, who embraces the shoulder, for the joint returns now quite well
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is outward, if the patient is conscious, as we have said concerning hiccup, and is strangulated, that is to say that the limb is stretched out above the affected limb and on the foot also.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two thumbs, one at the head and the other at the foot, and grasp the thumb between the thighs of the patient in the form of an arc
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and has spread wet cloths around, so that it does not bleed the patient, then extend the limbs ministering to him, and look with your hands that the dislocation is even.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, it is well. If not, put on the table and press on it as we said in the previous case, and keep the patient lying on the side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When the dislocation is forward, if it is possible, extend the limb slightly, as we have said; and keep the patient’s gaze fixed on the painful area, and press at the other hand, and extend downwards towards the groin.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	When the dislocation is backwards, if it is not possible to extend the limb backwards, do not lift it from the ground, but rather keep it as it is, because if you lift it up backwards it will be further damaged, as we have said above concerning the two inches of the armpit.</start_of_turn
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And if it is on the face, and the limb is extended as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And will be at a point when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; then hold the knees, put the support, and strain of a bandage, so that the hair does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And rest for two or three days, then loosen it, and put the support on; and if you see that they are even, if you strain as before, and leave it. For two days; then loosen it, and do it gently, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation from the shoulder-blade.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is swollen in two ways: from within and from behind; and do not pull forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that if you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and it does not reach their buttock, the swelling is in the buttock; if it does reach their buttock, the swelling has gone down
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and if you make them sit down the patient, and extend their leg if they can, and put your hand on their face and your foot on their feet
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee at your palms, and pull in between your shoulders, then bend the two knees that make the knee; and another attendant extends their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that their leg is properly bent at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And place the bandage upon, and keep the limb raised to the hip, and bind them firmly together for two or three days; then remove it.  Do not let the patient move until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the limb is not in its place, if an extension is administered strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of dislocation.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The talons never is measured, and never is fully evacuated, and always is swollen and painful.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is if the ankle is dislocated, and try before to the part where it is displaced:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is dislocated, and try before to the part where it is displaced: if it can be moved easily, extend it gently with your hands when it is only slightly displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is thoroughly dislocated, it is prudent to make the patient sit upright, and hold him securely by the limb under the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take hold of the limb at your right hand, and then at the left hand once, and then extend it upwards, and keep it well stretched out;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	And do this thrice, as we have said, at the end and at the root of the limb; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the work, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	And if it cannot return, make the patient sit upright on the ground, and take hold of one leg firmly in the ground between his thighs, and cover him with a sheet, that he does not bleed the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then hold the limb still, and another attendant should extend the limb at his hands or at one of his joints, which should lie on the collar of the limb;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the chest muscles equally, and bind them either above or below the knees of the patient to hold the patient when stretching.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the eyes equally over the dislocation, and another assistant grasps the limb firmly at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it has reached a point, if you place the dressing and bandage above, and strain, and bind the limb to the leg, and keep the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that they are not too tight;
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for one or two days, and if the swelling subsides, strain; then unbind at the third or fourth hour, and uncover the patient for three days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if it goes before this end, it is not certain that it will not damage the other side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it persists, it is necessary to know that it must be appeased, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des dois	otherwise
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When they are dislocated, if they are properly repositioned without resistance, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not in the neck or the buttocks, command the patient to sit upright on a chair or table, and place your hand on the area where these joints open, then press your hand firmly until it returns to its place.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When it is even and there is no swelling, if you put the hand of the arm on a table at the armpits, then press firmly, and leave it for two days, then remove it; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It is from wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound occurs with the dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it has happened that the patient has died.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you do not cautiously presume in the cure, and you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not merciful, compassionate, and timely, do not attempt it;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use at the beginning calming things and cauterize the abscess, and let the patient hold the hand of God, if you do not see hope of healing;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you now reset the limb, even though the abscess remains;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is whole, if necessary, administer calming things around the wound, and cure the wound, if possible, with dried oils.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if the dislocation has burst, and bones are loose, if the bones are firm, do what we have said in simple ailments;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And take heed of entering into fear, as I have said, for this brings harm to your soul according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your body and your spirit. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Praise be to the physical body.
